Yesterday's Ningbo Association Urged Fish Merchants to Join the Fish Market, Agreeing to Join Under the Principle of Equal Treatment, Cooperative Methods to Be Further Discussed by Mediators 117

The entanglement between the fish market and the thirteen fish merchants who have not joined the fish market, after the Ningbo Association in Shanghai and the Chamber of Commerce successively urged them, the fish merchants have already resumed business. Now the Ningbo Association, in response to a telegram from the Ministry of Industry, requested the association to be responsible for urging the fish merchants to join the fish market for cooperation. Therefore, at 4 pm yesterday, the association convened representatives of the thirteen fish merchants at the association's premises on Xizang Road to urge them. The details are recorded below.

Representatives Present

The fish merchant representatives who attended yesterday included lawyer Shen Shanrong, Xu Shanxing of Taichang, Zhang Xiaochu of Hefeng, Chen Ruilin of Yuanchang, Wang Gengmao of Hongyuan, Wang Rongsheng of Dechang, Shi Jiaxiang of Gongda, Liu Tongde of Dacheng, Zheng Yunsheng of Shengji, Zhang Yinsheng of Yuantong, Liu Jingli of Qianfeng, Li Shide of Gongshun, Xu Yang of the Ice Fish Industry Association, and mediators Yu Qiaqing, Fang Jiaobo, Jin Tingsun, Kui Yanfang, etc., totaling seventeen people.

Agreement to Join

Chairman Yu Qiaqing conducted earnest guidance, and as a result, the representatives of the fish merchants, under the principle of demanding equal treatment with the fish merchants who had already joined, agreed to join the fish market for cooperation. It was further agreed that the association would first formally send a letter expressing their agreement to join, which would then be forwarded to the fish market for notification. The fish market would then send a letter of welcome, and then the mediators Yu Qiaqing, Yu Zuoting, Jin Tingsun, Kui Yanfang, Fang Jiaobo, Zhang Shenzhi, and other six people would convey the opinions of the fish merchants and discuss the cooperative methods in detail with the supervisory committee of the fish market. The meeting concluded at nearly 6 pm and was adjourned.

Method of Persuasion

After the meeting, Yu Qiaqing, Chairman of the Association, in his own name, issued a letter to the Municipal Ice Fish Industry Association, stating, "Respectfully, your association's colleagues, regarding the fish market matter, our association is well aware of the difficult situation of your colleagues. Now, for the sake of the overall situation, we sincerely hope that your association will quickly inform your thirteen colleagues. It is deeply beneficial. Therefore, we specially send this letter of persuasion, hoping you will investigate and act accordingly and reply. To the Shanghai Municipal Ice Fish Industry Association."

Original Telegram from the Ministry of Industry

To Mr. Yu Qiaqing of the Ningbo Association in Shanghai, Xizang Road: I have received your telegram. However, if the merchants do not join the fish market, they may have no business to do. Please, in the position of the association, quickly urge them to participate in the market. Many of the ice fish brokers in the market are from Ningbo, and we hope they will cooperate. Please reply. Ministry of Industry.

The Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Movement Committee of the Shanghai Lawyers Association hosted guests from local newspapers, radio stations, entertainment circles, and theaters at the East Hall on the ninth floor of the YMCA at Baxianqiao in the French Concession at 7 pm last night. Those present included He Jia, Guan Jiu'an, Hu Zhengzhi, Liu Hang, Chen Dabei, Wang Wanbai, and dozens of others. Committee members present included Zhang Shijie, Zhu Yakui, Qian Jianqiu, Dong Chi, Zha Renwei, Cai Huan, Ma Shouhua, Xu Zuoliang, Zhu Fuju, Yu Chengxiu, Zhang Runmin, Mao Yun, Shen Yingshi, Zhang Juansheng, Wu Zhenghe, Feng Xizui, Qu Yue, Sun Zuji, Yang Minshi, Yu Zhongluo, Chen Zhichi, Jin Ximin, Wang Wei, etc., who were warmly received by Wu Xuepeng, Dai Jixian, etc. After taking their seats, Yu Chengxiu, Zhongluo, etc. briefly described the significance of urging the government to formulate a wrongful imprisonment compensation law as soon as possible, and requested all circles to expand publicity on the Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Movement Day on June 7, in order to achieve the goal of implementing the wrongful imprisonment compensation law as soon as possible. The guests and hosts enjoyed the evening. The "Main Points of Publicity for the Entertainment Industry in the Wrongful Imprisonment Compensation Movement of the Shanghai Lawyers Association" are recorded below: "Dear listeners, this program is entrusted by the Shanghai Lawyers Association to say a few words about the wrongful imprisonment compensation matter, which is beneficial to the public and which the government is eagerly expected to realize immediately. An ancient saying goes, 'When a woman of Qi suffers injustice, it does not rain for three years; when Zou Yan is imprisoned, snow falls in June.' These two sentences mean that if there is injustice in prison, even heaven and earth will be enraged. How can knowledgeable and spirited human beings stand by and watch without helping? What is the way to help? It is that the people demand that the government formulate a law on wrongful imprisonment compensation as soon as possible. The wrongful imprisonment compensation law stipulates that the judicial authorities, due to the exercise of their powers, unjustly imprison people, and they must bear the responsibility for compensation. To say it again, for officials serving in the judicial authorities, we want them to compensate for the spiritual or material losses of those who are unjustly imprisoned without cause. This system has been practiced for a long time in foreign countries. Since ancient times, our country has been extremely cautious in judging cases. There are 'those who indulge and deliberately enter people into crimes should bear joint responsibility,' (note: that is, officials who connive and deliberately implicate people in crimes should bear joint responsibility), and the Tang Dynasty had 'whipping for violating judgments,' (note: one of the five punishments, using bamboo to strike, commonly known as the small board). Emperor Gaozong of the Song Dynasty 'gave money and rice needed for returning home to those who are innocent.' The classics are magnificent and easy to follow. The Republic of China has been established for twenty-five years. Everyone shouts slogans of respecting humanity and protecting human rights, but in reality, there are no provisions in the law for those who are unjustly imprisoned without cause to seek redress. Therefore, the Shanghai Lawyers Association holds a wrongful imprisonment compensation movement on a certain day in June every year. Why in June? Because June in the lunar calendar is around the Dragon Boat Festival, when families make zongzi to commemorate Qu Yuan, who was unjustly wronged and drowned himself in the river. It is hoped that the public will pay attention and unite to demand that the government quickly formulate a wrongful imprisonment compensation law, so as to avoid judicial officials from casually judging people to be sued and suffer losses. If we ordinary people unfortunately suffer unjust lawsuits and losses, with the wrongful imprisonment compensation law, we can also demand compensation from the state, etc."

Instructions from the Ministry of Finance: Method of Affixing Stamps to Remittance Receipts Should Be Handled According to Silver Money Receipts 123

Yesterday, the Ministry of Finance issued a directive to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce regarding the affixing of stamps to remittance receipts according to silver money receipts, stating: "Both Gengqing's telegrams have been received. Upon investigation, a remittance receipt is a receipt for receiving a remittance and is different in nature from a deposit receipt of a financial institution. According to the second item of the stamp tax rate table, silver money receipts, regardless of the amount, should be affixed with a two-cent stamp. Deposit receipts of financial institutions refer to the documents issued by financial institutions to depositors for withdrawing their deposits. A remittance receipt is a document established after receiving a certain amount of silver money remitted by a bank from a certain place. The former contains the nature of withdrawing silver money and should belong to the scope of withdrawing or remitting silver money in the fourth item of the tax rate. The latter contains the nature of receiving silver money and should belong to the scope of silver money and goods receipts in the second item of the tax rate table. In order to avoid misunderstandings by financial institutions, the words 'except for deposit receipts of financial institutions' are stated in the nature of the second item of the tax rate. Article 14 of the Implementing Rules of the Stamp Tax Law also clarifies the meaning of excluding deposit receipts of financial institutions. The provisions of the tax law are very clear. However, many banks in various places have printed the position for affixing stamps and the words 'two cents' on remittance receipts, which is based on the tax rate of the remittance receipt printed in the 'Questions on Affixing Stamps' compiled by the Banking Association. However, it is not known that the book was compiled by the Banking Practice Research Association affiliated to the association, and is intended for the study of banking colleagues and the general public. There are many errors in it and it is not sufficient to be used as a basis. How to affix stamps to vouchers used by the silver money industry should be based on the Stamp Tax Law. Since there are misunderstandings in various places, they should be corrected immediately. The Ministry has issued orders to the stamp tax bureaus of various provinces to instruct the banking associations of each province to notify all banks that remittance receipts should be affixed by the receiver according to the tax rate stipulated in the second item of the tax rate table. A one-cent stamp should be affixed for amounts of 3 yuan or more, a two-cent stamp for amounts of 10 yuan or more, and a three-cent stamp for amounts of 100 yuan or more. The receiver must not be required to affix a two-cent stamp regardless of the amount, and the words 'two cents' printed on the receipt should be deleted to comply with the tax law. As for the previous remittance receipts sent by banks for which the receiver should have affixed a three-cent stamp but only affixed a two-cent stamp, if it is verified that the words 'two cents' are indeed printed on the receipt, then the receiver's underpayment of the stamp tax is due to misunderstanding and should be leniently exempted from further investigation. Otherwise, the receiver should still be responsible. In addition to consulting the provincial and municipal governments to order the governments of each city and county to instruct the staff of the provincial stamp tax bureaus to inform them all, you should be informed of this batch."

Various Industries Agree to Reform the Accounting Year-End Opinions 125

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, yesterday, the government intended to change the accounting year to a calendar year system, and then transferred the opinions of various industries to Mr. Wei Tingsheng of the Legislative Yuan. The letter stated that it had received your letter inquiring whether it would be inconvenient for merchants and people if the government's accounting year was changed to a calendar year system. On May 23, we first answered with a summary of our association's opinions, and later received replies from the restaurant industry, insurance industry, egg industry, cotton trading industry, etc., and forwarded them on May 29. Now we have received letters from Hua soap industry, pawn industry, and inland river shipping industry, stating that the government's use of the calendar year system as the accounting year is not inconvenient for merchants and people. The medicine industry also stated that the government's current accounting year is rarely used in commerce except for banks, and still follows the commercial customs of receiving and resolving to conclude. This situation has been understood by the government, so whether the government's accounting year is changed or not in the future is not of much importance, etc. The meaning is the same as the association's reply on May 23. This is the general situation of the commercial industry in the city. Now, because the ten-day deadline set in your letter has expired, the intentions of the various industries that replied later are the same as the various letters now, and there is no discrepancy, so they will no longer be forwarded to avoid redundancy and are combined for statement.

The National Federation of Commerce Emailed the Ministry of Finance Requesting to Stop Affixing Stamps to Purchase Drafts, the Jiangxi Stamp Tax Bureau Misunderstood the Department's Regulations, Requesting to Issue a Notice to Stop Disputes 126

Yesterday, the National Federation of Commerce emailed the Ministry of Finance, stating: "Recently, the Jiujiang Chamber of Commerce sent a letter stating that many cases of forcing the affixing of stamps to foreign purchase drafts have been discovered in Jiujiang this year, causing extreme disturbance. The reason for the mandatory affixing of stamps is that this bill is a bill for withdrawing goods and should be handled according to the fifth item in the tax rate table, which is an over-misunderstanding. Bills for withdrawing goods are for paying goods by voucher, without any increase or decrease, and have a definite value as proof, so stamps should be affixed. This purchase order, for the party issuing the order, some are dedicated to stores with whom they have dealings, and some are not related to any specific store. Regardless of the number of goods opened on the order, and the amount of silver dollars attached, it is only to let the other party know the number of goods needed for details. After the other party receives the order, whether the goods are complete and the price is as required, those who have dealings must register and account according to their actual situation, and those who have no dealings must issue an invoice according to their actual situation and hand it over to the purchaser as proof. The purchaser's original draft has no effect of withdrawing goods and is absolutely insufficient to be given importance. The nature should be clarified and the Ministry of Finance should be asked to order the bureau to cancel this stamp affixing, etc. Upon investigation, the nature of the shipping invoice in the first item and the bill for withdrawing goods in the fifth item in the stamp tax law tax rate table are very clear and should not be stretched. It is said that if all purchase drafts are required to be affixed with stamps, then the store receiving the order must go through the shipping procedures again after receiving the order, regardless of whether the goods and prices opened on the order are exactly the same. This is stamping twice for one item at one time. Considering the legislative intent and the names of the tax rates, in addition to directly submitting a report to the Ministry of Finance, asking for an order to the Jiangxi Stamp and Tobacco Tax Office to cancel this stamp affixing, the corresponding letter is sent to your association, asking you to investigate and forward it to the Ministry of Finance for vigorous struggle to achieve the goal of cancellation, etc. According to this reason, it is appropriate to email to your department for review, and ask for permission to issue a notice to stop the universal exemption of purchase drafts from stamp affixing, to avoid disputes. Chairman of the National Federation of Commerce of the Republic of China, Lin Kanghou."

Mr. Mao Zhongfang, Military Counselor and Director of the Bureau of Ceremonies of the National Government, recently fell ill in Shanghai and was admitted to the West Shanghai Sanatorium for treatment. Mr. Mao was from Minhou, Fujian. In his early years, he ran around for the revolution, abandoned his naval studies, and was a pioneer in the party-state's naval circles. When studying in the United Kingdom, he served as an officer on a British warship and was highly regarded by the people of that country. Later, he was summoned back to China by Admiral Sa Zhenbing to serve as the highest naval coach. During the Xinhai Revolution, he joined forces with the martyr Chen Qimei to launch an uprising and served as the commander-in-chief of the navy. He retired after success. After that, he followed the Premier and did not serve in local positions. He is now in this position and is relied upon by Chairman Lin. But before he reached the age of sixty, he passed away suddenly. The bad news spread and Chairman Lin and others mourned him greatly and sent telegrams of condolences. Today, the maple forest bridge must be decorated with plain cars and white horses, and be full of sorrow.

Shedding the Uniform to Cease the Ferocity: Adultery Exposed, Plotting a Response; Chinese Constable Opens Fire, Killing a Man; Driven by Fury, a Second Landlord Rushes Over, Opening Fire and Fatally Wounding Him; The Murderer, Zhang Junmou, Is Also Captured by Detectives, Suffering Gunshot Wounds; The Adulterous Woman Breaks Down in Tears Upon Seeing Her Lover Injured. 132

Yesterday morning, around 5 AM, a tragic bloodbath occurred at No. of Tonghe Lane, 218 Foch Road, in the Public Concession. The deceased was Jiao Guisun, the second landlord of the house, and his wife, Mrs. Jiao, was also severely wounded. The perpetrator of this crime was Zhang Junmou (30 years old), a Chinese constable with badge number 2650 from the Huishan Police Station, originally from Anhui Province. However, during the incident, Zhang Junmou was also shot and wounded by Chinese constables from both the British and French concessions. The

Trial Proceedings are recorded in detail below. First, the police lawyer, Zhang Tianyin, gave a detailed account of the incident, stating that Wu Yujing, a man from Anhui Province, currently 43 years old, works as a driver of vehicle No. 214 at the Foch Road branch of the Xiang Sheng Motor Company. He married Wu Chen, a woman from the same province, over ten years ago, and they resided on the third-floor mezzanine of Jiao Changgui's house at No. 3 Tonghe Lane, Foch Road, raising four daughters. The eldest is ten years old, and the youngest is only eight months old and still in swaddling clothes. The first defendant, Zhang Junmou, has been a Chinese constable with badge number 2650 at the Huishan Police Station for ten years. Because he and the Wu couple were from the same province and had known each other for a long time, they had frequent interactions. Later, Zhang discovered that Wu Chen felt her husband and Yujing were old, and she deeply

regretted her beauty being wasted on an old man. Therefore, he seized the opportunity to make advances. Soon, he achieved his goal, and their affair had become frequent. On the 27th of last month, Wu Yujing returned home from the company, only to find his wife and Zhang Junmou whispering sweet nothings in the living room, behaving intimately. Zhang immediately left when he saw Wu. Since then, Zhang, fearing that his affair had been exposed by Wu, discussed running away with Wu Chen. The next day, the 28th, she packed up valuables worth 110 yuan and fled. Wu Yujing then reported the situation to the Chengdu Road Police Station, stating that his wife had run away with Zhang Junmou. After receiving the report, the police dispatched detectives to the Huishan Police Station to inquire about Zhang, but since there was no corroborating evidence, they took

no action at the time. Until about 5 AM this morning, Chinese constable Zhang Junmou, badge number 2650, was supposed to be on night duty on Huishan Road as usual. Unexpectedly, after only one hour on duty, he went to Room 26 of the Tiande Inn on Dalian Bay Road. He knocked on the door and entered the house, announcing to Wu Yujing, "I have no personal animosity towards you, but please ask Jiao Changgui to come downstairs." Since Jiao refused to come downstairs, Zhang went upstairs and fired four shots, severely wounding the Jiao couple. Zhang immediately

took the gun and went downstairs, attempting to flee. He was shot eight times by Chinese constables No. 127, No. 914, No. 885 from the Chengdu Road Police Station, and No. 658 from the French Police Station, wounding his left shoulder and causing him to fall to the ground. At that time, Wu Chen, seeing Zhang injured, immediately went forward and cried bitterly. She was then arrested. Telegrams were sent to the police station, and detectives were dispatched to send the injured to the hospital for treatment. However, Jiao Changgui soon died. Mrs. Jiao's injuries are severe, and her life is in danger. Therefore, we request that Wu Chen be detained, etc." When questioned, Wu Chen confessed to having an affair with Zhang Junmou for only one month. On the 28th of last month, I ran away from home and spent the night with Zhang at the Shihua Hotel. The next day, we moved to the Tianqing Hotel. Last night, Zhang returned to the hotel, saying that the

secret had been exposed, that your husband had reported it to the police, and that Jiao "Ma Pí" (i.e., Changgui) from the front building had testified. It would be better to send you back, but Jiao should not ruin my good deeds. In the future, we must find a way to kill him. We discussed it all night, and at 5 AM this morning, Zhang hired a Gonghe car and accompanied me to Tonghe Lane. I only went to the downstairs of No. 3, but Zhang had already acted upstairs, etc." Wu Yujing also stated in his report that he was 43 years old, from Anhui Province, and worked as a driver for the Xiang Sheng Motor Company. He lived with his wife, Chen, on the second-floor mezzanine of No. 3 Tonghe Lane. On the 28th of last month, my wife ran away, and according to Jiao Changgui, it was related to Zhang Junmou. So, on the 31st, I reported it to the police. This morning, around 4 AM, Zhang and Wu Chen

arrived and called at the door. After my friend, surnamed Ma, opened the door, Zhang and others demanded the evidence that I had reported them for adultery. Seeing their aggressive manner, I fled to a nearby company. Unexpectedly, Zhang and others followed and entangled with me. Unable to do anything, I took the opportunity to drive an empty car to the police station to report. By the time I returned home with the detectives, the tragedy had already occurred, etc." Jiao Changgui's ten-year-old son, Dingqiao, also testified that he saw Zhang at the door, first shooting his mother twice, causing her to fall to the ground, and then shooting his father twice, killing him. Mr. Qiu Chunshan, Owner of the Chunhua Silk Braid Factory in the Nanshi District, Assassinated. 134

Three Assailants Inflict Multiple Ax Wounds, Leaving Him in Critical Condition; Leaflets Found Afterward Offer Potential Clues.

Qiu Chunshan, 43, from Zhenjiang, resides at No. 9, Jiande Lane, Scissors Bridge, Meixie Road, Nanshi. He has been running the Chunhua Silk Braid Factory at the Huining Road intersection for over ten years, and the business is quite prosperous. He is known for being amiable and capable and also serves as the chairman of the Nanshi Rickshaw Industry Association. He is married to Mrs. Cao, 40, and they have three sons and three daughters, enjoying a comfortable life and family happiness. Recently, Qiu purchased land

to build a new five-room house at the Lingjia Residence on Meixie Road, which will be completed soon. He planned to move the Chunhua Silk Braid Factory there. Yesterday morning at 7 AM, Qiu left his home and went to the Lingjia Residence to inspect the new house. At 8:30 AM, as he was about to return home for breakfast, he was ambushed by three assailants while passing through the wasteland west of Chezhan Road, near the Jiangbei Great World. One of the assailants was tall and burly, wearing a blue cloth long gown, while the other two were wearing blue cloth short jackets. They blocked his path, and each of them drew a sharp ax, attacking Qiu fiercely. He was struck in the left leg, suffering a severe ax wound, and also received five ax wounds to his right arm, front, and back chest. He collapsed in a pool of blood, barely breathing. Upon hearing the news, officers from the Liyuan Road and Chezhan Road police stations rushed to the scene, but the assailants had already fled. He was immediately sent to Shanghai Hospital for treatment and admitted to Ward 22.

Due to excessive blood loss, his life is in critical condition. Subsequently, Yao Guangnai, the chief of the Ximen Branch Bureau, ordered detective Yao Renjie to go to the scene of the attack to investigate the incident. Two printed leaflets related to the case were found nearby. The titles were "China Industrial and Commercial Patriotic Youth Association" and "Shanghai Comrades Organization Secret Investigation Squad," etc. Therefore, the truth behind the attack may be related to these organizations. The police station is now working hard to investigate and strictly apprehend the perpetrators and bring them to justice. After Qiu Chunshan arrived at the hospital, he underwent surgery and bandaging. As of 8 PM last night, he was still conscious. If his condition does not change, his life can be saved.

Frequent Public Bus Accidents; Judge Advocates for Caution 135

Gu Yongxiang's Corpse Examined Yesterday; Driver Under Investigation by Police

Gu Yongxiang, a 15-year-old student from a certain middle school, residing at No. 18 Shanxi Road, along with three classmates, were riding bicycles out of Yongning Lane on Henan Road around 9 AM the day before yesterday. Unexpectedly, Shi Zhenggao, the driver of public bus No. 15037 on Route 5, was also driving south on the same road. Unable to avoid a collision, the front right wheel of the bus knocked Gu over, and both the person and the bicycle were run over by the wheel, causing Gu severe injuries. After the police arrived, they urgently summoned an ambulance and rushed him to the hospital for treatment, but it was ineffective, and he died shortly after. Upon receiving the report, the chief patrol officer ordered detective Yang Zaishan and others to investigate the scene. The body was then transported to the Feilun Road morgue. Yesterday, Zhang Zongru, a prosecutor from the First Special District Court, along with two forensic doctors, Wei and Zhang, and clerk Wang Zuyi, arrived at the morgue to examine the body. First, the Western police chief reported the situation, stating that the deceased was riding his bicycle out of Yongning Lane and intended to turn south. He should have made a small turn, but at that time, a rickshaw was parked at the entrance of the lane. To pass the rickshaw, he made a large turn. A rickshaw was also on the opposite side of the road, causing the public bus to hit him, etc. Gu Kaishi, 55, a cook, also stated that the deceased was his son and that he was killed in the accident, requesting justice. Prosecutor Zhang stated that there were many public bus accidents in Shanghai and instructed the Western police chief that someone from the court witnessed the public bus swerving too far to the right at the time of the accident, and that the perpetrators must be warned in the future. He then announced that the examination confirmed that the deceased, student Gu Yongxiang, male, was indeed knocked down and run over by public bus No. 15037 on Route 9, resulting in his death. The body was handed over to the deceased's father, Gu Kaishi, for burial after signing a bond. The bus driver, Shi Zhenggao, was at fault for swerving to the right while driving and should be investigated by the police.

The Origin of the Box Cannon Under the Coffin 136

Originally Hidden by a Robbery Gang; The Thief Has Reformed and Turned to Good.

The Zhabei Xinzha Branch of the Shanghai Public Security Bureau received a tip-off at the end of last month that a box cannon and other items were hidden under a coffin somewhere in Tanzi Bay. The branch chief, Liao Jiongran, immediately dispatched the on-duty police chief, Zhu Jiapu, along with detectives Zang Nai, Zhang Shuwen, Lü Qingkang, and Yang Yucai, to investigate. They found a box cannon wrapped in a black raincoat and 26 bullets under a coffin on a barren tomb. The number on the gun was 741001. After bringing it back to the bureau, Branch Chief Liao believed that the report was not without connection, so he immediately ordered the report to be investigated and verified. It has been learned that the box cannon was owned by Huang Tie, a robber who committed a crime in the Public Concession and was sentenced to eight years in prison. While serving his sentence in the Huade Road Prison, he met Sun Dejin (also a thief). In January of this year, Huang was released on parole after serving only three years. Later, Sun was also paroled and bailed out by someone. Recently, Sun suddenly encountered Huang on the road. Upon seeing each other, they were very friendly because they were fellow inmates and invited Huang to Sun's home in a thatched shed in Tanzi Bay for a chat before parting. The next evening around 9 PM, Huang brought a box cannon and 26 bullets to Sun's house for temporary storage. Sun, having already reformed and turned to good, refused to accept them. However, Huang insisted on temporarily placing them there, and there was a slight conflict in their words. Later, Sun feared that something unfavorable might happen to him, so he took the box cannon and bullets and told Huang to come and take them the next day. Unexpectedly, Huang did not come to retrieve them the next day, so Sun Dejin hid the box cannon under a coffin behind the land temple next to the nearby cattle bone factory and secretly reported it to the Xinzha Branch Bureau to be retrieved. It is now known that Branch Chief Liao believes that since the criminal committed a crime in the Public Concession and was released on parole, there must have been a guarantee. Who is the guarantor? It is not difficult to investigate. If the criminals can repent and surrender, turn to good, they can be forgiven for the past.

Wang Fengzhen Sues College Student for 8,000 Yuan in Compensation 137

Investigating Shen Jinzhi's Age; Was There Coercion Involved if Love Letters Led to Seduction?

Shen Jinzhi, the young owner of the Shen Wanyu lamp wick and rush mat shop at No. 327 Yongyou Lane, Damatou Road, Nanshi, enjoys the blessings of his ancestors and is wealthy. He spends his nights in brothels and is a handsome young man, a "小白臉" (pretty boy) of Shanghai. Therefore, he is well-liked by prostitutes. Several years ago, he became close to Wang Fengzhen, a Yunnan style courtesan in the area between Guangxi Road and Shantou Road. They extinguished the candles and left their hair unbound, and made vows with bitten arms, eventually agreeing to marry each other and even taking a photo together at Tiger Hill in Suzhou. Since Shen was unmarried at home, the two planned to become a legal couple. However, Shen's family strongly opposed it, so they once drew up an agreement to separate. However, in the winter of last year, their old love revived, and the two drew up a contract themselves, stating that if the man abandoned the woman, he would have to compensate her 8,000 yuan. If the woman left the man, she would have to compensate him 5,000 yuan. However, due to family pressure and the shifting of money, Shen Jinzhi, on April 19 of this year, followed his parents' wishes and held a wedding with Xia Hefang, a wealthy woman, at the Lake Society Auditorium. Wang Fengzhen, seeing that her lover had become a stranger, took the contract to the Shanghai District Court, requesting a judgment ordering the payment of 8,000 yuan in compensation according to the contract. The lawsuit stated that Shen Jinzhi was currently 22 years old, and Wang Fengzhen was also 22 years old. This case continued to be heard yesterday. Shen Jinzhi raised the issue of age, stating that he was only 21 years old at the time and that he had not yet celebrated his birthday when the contract was made, meaning that he was still under 20 years old, and therefore had no capacity to act under the law. He also claimed that the contract was made at the Daya Restaurant, where he was made drunk and taken to the China Hotel, where he was forced to write it by more than ten men and women, and that it was not of his own free will. However, Wang Fengzhen said that Shen was a college student and was actually 22 years old, and that there were love letters seducing her before the contract was made, so how could there be coercion? The court ordered that the age be clarified before further hearing.

Lin Tianji Accused of Seduction and Abandonment 138

Court Summons Plaintiff for Questioning Yesterday; Jing Youmei Provides Details of the Seduction

Lin Tianji, the deputy director of the Audit Office of the Central Bank, from Guangdong, was recently accused by Jing Kekong, the father of Jing Youmei (21 years old, originally from Nanjing, moved to Wuxing), a woman from Wuxing who previously studied at Peiming Girls' High School on Magen Road, of seducing and abandoning his daughter. After receiving the lawsuit, the court believed that the facts listed in the plaintiff's lawsuit were unclear, so Judge Xiao Bianfen opened the Criminal Division 3 at 2 PM yesterday, and summoned only the plaintiff, Jing Kekong, and the person concerned, Jing Youmei, to be questioned. The defendant, Lin Tianji, was not notified. Jing Kekong stated that he lived at No. 412 Jingjiang Road and worked as a staff member in the Ganyu County government. My daughter was born at the hour of Xu on September 12-13 of the Republic of China Year 4, the year of the Dragon. Although she is nominally 21 years old, she is actually not yet 20 years old. As for the facts of the seduction, you must ask my daughter, etc. The court then summoned Jing Youmei to the case. According to her testimony, in August of the Republic of China Year 22, I came to Shanghai with my mother and lived at No. 5 Pingqiao Lane, Aivenyi Road. I went to Peiming Girls' High School to register for admission. I met my friend, Shen Xifan, at the registration office and went to Sincere Company with her to shop. I met Lin at the company. From then on, he rented No. 20 Ruikang Lane, Beijing Road, and we lived together. I told my mother that I could not stay at home because I was busy with schoolwork and traveling for sightseeing, in order to deceive her. Later, we moved to Anning Lane, Hercux Road. In January of Year 23, my mother found out because I was pregnant. Lin said that he would marry me after I gave birth, so my mother did not negotiate with him. I then gave birth to a son, who is now three years old. On July 1 of last year, we moved to No. 83 Baoshan Lane. I currently live there. At first, Lin gave me 150 yuan per month for living expenses, but in February of this year, it was reduced to 100 yuan, and last month it was reduced to 70 yuan. Now he has stopped coming altogether, and I have learned that he already has a wife. My father has also found out, so I filed a lawsuit. Judge Xiao asked in great detail about the location, time, and details of the cohabitation, and then ordered them to withdraw and await verification.

The Yan and Guo Families Dispute Over Lost Child Due to Mistaken Identity 139

Although Faces Are Similar, Child Claims Surname Is Yan, Not Guo.

Grandma Yan Ding, from Suzhou, lives at No. 53 Lin Yin Branch Road. She had a son named Gengquan, who has passed away, leaving behind a seven-year-old grandson, Guanqing. In June of the year before last, he was abducted by bandits. At the same time, Haiji, the four-year-old son of Guo Jinling from Beiping, was also abducted. Despite searching everywhere, there was no trace of them. It was not until September of last year that the Ruian Public Security Bureau in Zhejiang Province cracked an abduction case. They learned that the abducted child lived in Shanghai, so they photographed the child and sent it to the Shanghai Public Security Bureau, requesting that the family be contacted to identify him. Guo Jinling learned of this and went to identify him. He saw that the abducted child's face was similar to that of his lost four-year-old Haiji and was overjoyed. He rushed to Ruian overnight and took the child Guanqing back as Haiji. Unexpectedly, at the end of the year, a child living next door to Yan Ding's family passed by the Guandi Temple on Zhaojiabang Road and suddenly saw Guanqing, who had been missing for more than a year. He immediately ran to tell Yan Ding and embraced him as if he had found a rare treasure. He was about to ask him what had happened when Guo Jinling heard the news and rushed out, accusing Yan Ding of falsely claiming the lost child. He called the police, and they were both taken to the bureau and transferred to the District Court, where they were interrogated by Prosecutor Tang. Guo claimed that Guanqing was his abducted son, while the old woman claimed that he was her grandson, clearly showing that Guo had deliberately mistaken the child and taken him away. After the prosecutor's interrogation, and after listening to the child's statement and accent, it was proven that he was Yan Ding's grandson, and that Guo's lost child was four years old, while this child was seven years old. Therefore, Guanqing was given to Yan Ding to take care of. However, due to the strange appearance of the child, which was similar to that of Guo Jinling, he relied on the issue of appearance and filed a lawsuit in the civil court, demanding confirmation that Guanqing was his biological son Haiji. Yesterday, Judge Han Jingdou summoned him for questioning, and also summoned the neighbor cited by Yan Ding as a witness, and the child Guanqing was also brought to court. He also stated that he was not Guo's son, but Yan Ding's grandson, and that his name was Guanqing, not Haiji. The judge then announced the end of the interrogation and scheduled a date for the verdict.

The True Manuscript of Yue Zhongwu's Memorials. Yue Zhongwu was a national hero of our country, a military man who excelled in literature. His "Manjianghong" poem is widely known and loved, and his calligraphy also embodies the spirit of Lu Gong. However, only his stone inscriptions are commonly seen, and his true manuscripts are rarely circulated. Now, the Commercial Press has found the true manuscript of Zhongwu's memorials and reproduced it in a volume for the public. This true manuscript scroll is a treasure collected by Mr. Fang Mengyuan from Dingyuan, over three feet in length, with inscriptions from various eras. It is truly a masterpiece. Mr. Mengyuan was a famous collector of the Qing Dynasty and wrote "Mengyuan Shumu." During the Tongzhi and Guangxu periods, when he was the governor of Huai salt, he had Zhongwu's memorials engraved on stone to preserve them forever. Last autumn, the Commercial Press requested permission to reproduce it, and after ten months of work, the spirit and essence have been preserved without any loss. It will be available for sale soon.

Shanghai's Hardware Industry 156

— Edited by Zhongguo Hui

(Twenty-seventh Overview of Shanghai Industry and Commerce)

1. Evolution and Scope of the Hardware Industry

The history of Shanghai's hardware industry has no definite record. Except for the copper and tinware production, which began during the Tongzhi period, the so-called hardware industry has only about sixty years of history to date. According to reports, it started as peddling, and after Mr. Ye Chengzhong opened the Lao Shunfei Hardware Store (also known as food hardware at the time), Shanghai gradually had the name of the hardware industry. Subsequently, due to the progress of the world's mining and metallurgical industries, there were many products, and the patterns were also updated daily. Therefore, the scope of the hardware industry gradually expanded. Until today, everything from construction raw materials to doors, windows, and trivial utensils is included. The business is becoming increasingly complex, so the industry is divided according to the types of goods.

Commonly known as hardware includes gold, silver, copper, iron, and tin. Except for gold and silver, which are mainly used as currency and jewelry and have been separated and independently operated, the remaining copper, iron, and tin are very useful in industry. Machines, guns, bullets, building materials, and household utensils all depend on these. There are also lead, antimony, zinc, and nickel, which are listed outside of hardware, but their usefulness is not less than copper, iron, and tin, so they are usually included in the hardware industry. In terms of the size of the business scope, the industry can be divided into the following types: 1. Iron industry - selling steel bars, plates, and raw and cooked iron blocks for construction purposes.

2. Large hardware industry - selling construction metal materials, such as galvanized iron sheets, tinplate, steel bars, etc.

3. Small hardware industry - buying and selling metal products for roads, mines, factories, and daily odds and ends, such as knives, pins, springs, hinges, etc.

4. Copper and tin industry - specializing in hardware mineral raw materials, such as copper, tin, lead, antimony, nickel, zinc, and manufacturing and selling copper and tin household utensils.

In addition to the above four types, there are also those who manufacture machines and sell hardware parts, which are called machine hardware industry. Those who mainly deal in glass and attach small hardware are called glass hardware industry. Those who manufacture hardware accessories used on vehicles are called vehicle hardware industry. Those who undertake water and electricity projects and sell metal products such as water pipes and faucets are called electrical hardware industry. Those who buy and sell glassware and sell household cooking metal utensils are called food hardware industry. Those who sell architectural decorations such as carpets, painted cloths, oil felt bathtubs, etc. and hardware parts are called miscellaneous hardware industry. Those who buy and sell used hardware products are called used hardware industry. Taken together, it can be seen that the scope of the hardware industry is vast. However, the hardware industry in Shanghai refers to the iron industry, large hardware, small hardware, and steel and tin industries. In addition to the operation and sale of metal products, it is not a purely hardware industry (to be continued).

Special Issue for the June 3rd Memorial Held by All Sectors of Shanghai

Eliminating the Scourge of Opium and Transforming Life 157

— Wu Tiecheng

—Transcribed from a Speech During the Expanded Propaganda Week for Opium Prohibition and Drug Rejection—

Grand Preceptor Pulin said: "The poison of opium is more severe than floods and wild beasts. There is no one in the world who can say that opium should not be prohibited... If this disaster is not eliminated, in ten years, not only will there be no usable soldiers, but there will also be no funds to support them." The spread of opium in the mainland is like the spread of a boil on the body: today, the scourge of opium has spread, and it will not only be ten years, but perhaps a hundred years. The severity of the opium scourge is undoubtedly well known to everyone; even those who are addicted to opium deeply hate it. Why is it that for a hundred years, the more opium is prohibited, the more rampant the scourge becomes; even promising young people cannot prevent the invasion of opium? This is due to the incomplete, incomplete, and severe prohibition methods in the past. However, examining the most fundamental cause, it is due to the irrationality of the general national life. Wealthy families, idle crowds, do not engage in proper work or production; their lives are romantic and undisciplined, with no rules. Eating, living, and sleeping are irregular, and they are addicted to the pleasures of sensual gratification, indulging day and night, consuming and exhausting themselves, resulting in insufficient spirit and daily loss of energy. Therefore, they drink poison to quench their thirst, become addicted to opium, and cannot free themselves. Therefore, to eliminate the scourge of opium, on the one hand, we should seek thorough methods and strict laws; on the other hand, we should engage in the transformation of national life; so that the national life becomes more rational, and the people of the country are strong and vigorous; and no longer feel the need for opium. This is the fundamental way to eliminate the scourge of opium, and it is up to the active promotion of the New Life Movement!

The June 3rd Memorial and Lin Zexu 158

— Ma Liang

With foreign troubles increasing daily and national crises unresolved, on this June 3rd Memorial, we remember the sage Lin Zexu. Reflecting on the past, can our hearts not be filled with pain? Lin Zexu's far-sightedness and deep understanding of matters were unmatched in his time. When discussing the harm of opium, he said: "It is more severe than floods and wild beasts. Even Yao and Shun in today's world could not but eliminate it. The sage enforces the law to punish good, which is for the sake of the world for all generations, and no one in the world can say that opium should not be prohibited." "If this disaster is not eliminated, in ten years there will be no soldiers to use and no funds to raise." The spread of opium in the mainland is like the spread of ulcers on the body. When ulcers grow, they gradually become pus; when opium comes, it gradually leads to invaders..." As for the method of prohibiting opium, he advocated cutting off the source externally, requiring foreign merchants to sign a guarantee: "If opium is found to be carried in the future, the goods will be confiscated and the person will be executed." Internally, following Huang Weizi, he first advocated the use of strict laws and severe punishments: "The pain of quitting addiction is worse than cangues and imprisonment. The offender knows this and refuses to quit. If he is sentenced to death, the urgency of the execution is more painful than the prolongation of addiction..." As for the abstinence of addicts, he used the five-family mutual responsibility system for the people and the five-person mutual guarantee regulations for the soldiers. He first showed compassion, then threatened with punishment, explained the dangers, and encouraged with benefits, so that the people knew what to be vigilant about. In his explanation, there were awakened and painful words such as: "Wealth is the source of nourishing life, and silver is not easy to come by. To exchange silver for mud is ridiculous, and to give up silver to take poison is sad..." We can see that his observation was insightful, his arguments were just, his methods were meticulous, and his hatred was deep. Therefore, after being ordered to Guangzhou, vendors and addicts temporarily disappeared. He then forced British merchants to surrender more than 20,000 boxes of opium, which were burned on June 3, 1839. Because the Fushang merchants were aggressive, privately贩运, and did not submit, and even killed our people and refused to hand over the murderers, they borrowed the pretext of protecting overseas Chinese to cause the so-called Opium War, ceding land and paying indemnities, opening five ports for trade, and establishing the Treaty of Nanjing, which opened the precedent for concluding unequal treaties and causing endless troubles to the country. Before that, when the British ships opened fire on Guangdong, Lin Gong resisted the enemy and did not succeed; The border officials of the provinces, because of the long period of peace, were complacent, neglected to defend, did not understand the great righteousness, did not know how to unite, and gave way to treacherous people who loved profit and acted as accomplices, so the British army captured Dinghai, Zhejiang, leading to failure. As a result, Lin Gong was exiled, and the opium prohibition failed. He carried his ambition to the end! On this June 3rd Opium Prohibition Memorial Day, we remember the past and feel deeply saddened. Therefore, we introduce a brief history of Lin Gong to the people of the country, so that they can learn from his example and use it as a thought for reflection.

Early Years - His Life

Gong was born smart and quick. His body was short and his voice was loud. He married Zheng. His family had been scholars, but by the time of Gong, the family was in decline and food was often insufficient. He entered the village school at the age of four and never forgot what he read. He was recommended to the township at the age of twenty. Governor Zhang Shuicheng was surprised by him and invited him to be a guest, where he learned the essentials of criminal law and politics. At the age of twenty-seven, he became a jinshi and was appointed as an editor. He devoted himself to the study of statecraft and served as the examiner of Jiangxi and Yunnan. He was able to strictly eliminate the bad habits of the examination halls and earnestly select talents, and the atmosphere changed accordingly.

Middle Age - Promoting Water Conservancy, Dike Construction, Rectifying Money and Grain, and Cleaning up Officialdom

At the age of thirty-six, he was appointed as a supervising censor, and from then on, he began his political life. He considered everything related to national economy and people's livelihood. In particular, he was fair in judging cases, and the people praised him as "Lin Qingtian". His reputation for integrity was well-known. When he was summoned to the capital, Emperor Xuanzong praised him in person, saying, "Your reputation in Zhejiang is very good." From this, it can be seen that Gong was an upright official. In the third year of Daoguang, he was promoted to surveillance commissioner. At that time, Jiangsu suffered from floods, and the fields were devastated. Gong's father proposed various policies to relieve the famine, such as encouraging the county to distribute relief supplies, raising cattle for plowing, and burying the starving. Gong decided to implement them, and the people of Jiangsu congratulated him. He then became acting provincial administration commissioner, and his reputation was even greater. Before four years, Gong's parents passed away one after another. He was saddened and returned home. When he was out of office, he enjoyed the leisure of being at home. After serving his term of mourning, he repeatedly served as a provincial administration commissioner, governor-general, governor and other high-ranking officials, and vigorously eliminated the accumulated abuses of river works, reduced redundant personnel, exempted money and grain, rectified grain transportation, and consoled refugees. His achievements in benefiting the people were indeed not trivial. Emperor Xuanzong praised him, and he was transferred to five new positions in one year, which shows the emperor's favor.

Old Age - Handling Opium Prohibition

During the Daoguang Dynasty, foreign merchants shipped more than 30,000 boxes of opium to China every year, causing gold and silver to flow out and the people to become impoverished. The court officials advocated prohibiting opium to plug the leak and enrich the national treasury. Gong was based on his daily observations of the opium scourge and proposed six opium prohibition measures, and strongly advocated the death penalty. Because the opium scourge has reached its extreme, it cannot be prevented by ordinary methods. He also said, "It is not difficult to reform opium, but it is difficult to reform the heart. Therefore, if you want to reform the heart of playing with the law, how can you not establish a law of fear to make smokers wary and abstain themselves." After this memorial was submitted, he was ordered to Guangzhou for inspection and prohibition. On his way to office, Gong investigated the treacherous people who packaged, sold, transported, and escorted opium, and issued a notice to the Guangdong authorities to arrest them. As soon as he got off the bus, the old Yi merchant Chadun also fled back to his country first, and the bulk ships transporting opium were about to move away. Seeing this, Gong ordered the Yi merchants to quickly surrender the opium. The British leader and merchants were forced to agree to surrender, totaling more than 20,000 boxes, and ordered the British to issue a letter of guarantee that they would not transport opium again before they could complete the matter. On the one hand, he vigorously reorganized the military, trained strong men and repaired gun emplacements. He then received a court edict ordering the confiscation of opium to be destroyed on the spot. It was burned at Humen on June 3, 1839, and lasted for more than twenty days. Just then, an incident occurred in which a British man killed a Chinese man, and he refused to hand over the murderer. He then ordered the expulsion of the British from Macau and cut off firewood and food. The British leader was unwilling and fired at Kowloon to demonstrate. In view of this fierce situation, Gong flew to the capital. The Qing court then issued an edict formally suspending trade with British merchants and closing the port. The British were hit hard. When the British Parliament decided to send a fleet to China, it first attacked Guangdong and Fujian, and Gong planned to punish them severely. However, at that time, the people of the country were accustomed to comfort, and public opinion was boiling. They all said that Gong had rashly started an incident, which was not what they meant. Mrs. Zheng also advised him by letter, but she could not save Gong's determination to prohibit opium. He replied and explained his state of mind, saying: "Knowing that opium prohibition hinders the great interests of treacherous Yi and there will be difficulties, but I resolutely and resolutely dare not have any fear, because I have dedicated myself to the country, but I seek to benefit the country and the people, and to eliminate harm to the people. I have put my own life and death aside, and I do not care about praise or blame." From these few words, we can know Gong's hatred of opium and his resolute heart to resist aggression. The British army attacked Guangdong and Fujian and was unsuccessful, so it changed its attack to Dinghai and captured it. Because at that time, the coast had been empty for a long time, and the British side knew that the border officials of the other provinces of our country were ignorant of the times, neglected defense, had uneven steps, and lacked unity; and the court officials were afraid of disaster and blamed Gong. They sent Qi Shan to Guangdong for investigation and ordered the coastal border officials not to lightly fire on foreign ships and cause incidents. On the one hand, they still discussed Qi Shan's preparations for war. Who knew that Qi Shan was mediocre and cowardly, and everything was the opposite of what Gong had done. When he arrived in Guangdong, he completely withdrew the coastal defenses, dispersed the strong men, and abolished the navy, seeking peace with the British with all his heart. The British army took advantage of this opportunity to launch a large-scale attack. The Qing court was shocked and had no choice but to conclude the Treaty of Nanjing with the British, ceding Hong Kong, opening Guangzhou and five other ports for trade, and paying an indemnity of more than 20 million yuan. The opium scourge penetrated deep into the people.

Late Years - Intermittently Requesting Military Reclamation to Eliminate Ethnic Disputes Between Hui and Han

Gong's calligraphy resembles that of Ouyang Xun, and his poetry follows the style of Bai Juyi. When he was in office, he had no time to write poems, but when he was exiled to Yili, he was able to express his thoughts and also write letters, and people at the time imitated him. He stayed in Yili for nearly four years, opening up military reclamation for more than 370,000 hectares, which greatly improved the livelihood of the Hui people. When the general of Yili played a report, Emperor Xuanzong ordered him to act as the governor-general of Shaanxi and Gansu, and then appointed him as the governor. Unfortunately, he overworked himself, and his illness was deeply buried at this time. When he was transferred to the governor-general of Yunnan and Guizhou, he tried to release the ethnic boundaries between the same Han people and serve people with virtue. What is this? The customs of Yunnan are fierce, and bandits are rampant. Since Gong took office, he combined leniency and strictness, used both kindness and power, and the banditry was put down in a few months. The people were able to live in peace. However, since Mrs. Zheng's death, Gong was extremely sad: his old illness recurred, so he resigned and returned home. When he left, the people of Zheng carried wine to send him off, and tens of thousands of people gathered unexpectedly. The following year, Emperor Xuanzong died, and Emperor Wenzong ascended the throne. The Guangxi Hairi bandits started a rebellion, and ordered Gong to suppress it. He struggled to reach Chaozhou, and his diarrhea did not stop. He died in the Puning hostel. The heavens did not mourn, and he lost this pioneer in opium prohibition. The world's philosopher then left the world forever. Gong's great achievements will last forever, but it is a pity that the opium prohibition was not fully completed, and it should be regarded as a regret.

Since the establishment of our party, opium has been suspended as a prohibited item. The Premier also created a legacy of rejecting poison to show us, but in the past 20 years, warlords have been divided, and the environment is complex, so the prohibition policy has not been effective. Now, fortunately, our supreme leader Chairman Chiang Kai-shek has also served as the Opium Prohibition Supervisor, deeply fearing that opium is more than foreign insult. If this disaster is not eliminated, the nation will be difficult to rejuvenate, and the status of the country will be difficult to equalize; therefore, it is enforced vigorously and spared no effort, and stipulates various regulations such as a six-year phased prohibition method, and registration, reporting, and punishment to show compassion. Is it not the case that benevolence is practiced outside the law? We deeply hope that the national people will be vigilant, shuddering at the deep scourge of opium, look up to the government's intention to eliminate poison and do its best, work together, and watch its success, so that we will not fail Chairman Chiang's hard work as Opium Prohibition Supervisor, and the June 3rd Memorial Lin Gong will have true meaning.

Discussion of the Tobacco Prohibition Issue in This City 159

— Cai Jingjun

Since this city received orders last year to implement tobacco prohibition, the bureau has formulated a yearly plan for complete prohibition and earnestly promoted it with all its might. However, due to obstacles in jurisdiction and the special circumstances, implementation is difficult, quite different from other provinces. Unless the social conditions are carefully considered and prohibition standards are established, it will be difficult to adapt to the environment and achieve twice the result with half the effort. Now, several important issues regarding tobacco prohibition in this city are briefly outlined for discussion.

1. Emphasize Propaganda to Awaken Smokers: Our country's education is not yet universal, and the people are ignorant, to put it plainly. The working class in the lower strata of this city is numerous. The harm of tobacco and the content of laws are not easily understood by all the people. All sectors of society should pay special attention to propaganda and explain the meaning of tobacco prohibition. For example, the education sector should work hard to educate citizens in literacy, making tobacco prohibition an educational material. The press should take the lead in expressing opinions and guiding the public to engage in anti-drug movements. At the same time, social intellectuals should promote a new lifestyle, encouraging the public to abandon addictions and develop habits of diligence, thrift, and simplicity, fostering a deep hatred and abhorrence of tobacco. All these aspects are intended to enhance the strength of tobacco prohibition, relying on the cooperation of the people and the government to jointly promote it. We should know that the purpose of propaganda is to awaken smokers' automatic consciousness. It is better to use heart-reforming methods to enlighten their inner consciousness and encourage automatic cessation than to rely solely on strict laws and severe punishments to make people fear and dare not commit crimes. Since the bureau started registering smokers, surveys have shown that nearly ten thousand people in this city have quit smoking. Those who quit on their own account for half of that, which is not without the power of propaganda for tobacco prohibition policies. In the future, we should gather the strength of the entire population to step up propaganda to gradually reduce the number of smokers and achieve the goal of complete prohibition within a limited time.

2. Strictly Prohibit Smuggling to Eliminate the Source of Tobacco Poison: This city has never produced tobacco seedlings. The scope of prohibition is limited to transportation, sales, and smoking. Prohibiting transportation and sales is of utmost importance. If the source of smuggling and illegal sales is not stopped, there is no hope of eliminating tobacco poison. This city has convenient transportation, making it easy to smuggle goods. Unlawful individuals often take advantage of this opportunity to secretly set up dens, dodging here and there, making it impossible to defend against. The difficulty of prohibition reaches its extreme. Now that we are actively investigating and prosecuting tobacco poison, we should seek thorough prohibition methods. On the government side, responsible investigation personnel should study effective methods, unite with local and neighboring police authorities, take the same steps, and cooperate in investigation and prosecution. All transportation and navigation agencies should closely cooperate with investigation personnel to strictly prevent the entry of tobacco poison and order their employees to separately provide joint guarantees to avoid colluding with bandits for secret trafficking. On the public side, they should know that these criminals who transport and sell drugs not only undermine the prohibition policy but are also enemies of mankind. Anyone who hears or sees should act according to their conscience, take responsibility for reporting, and not provide housing for those who manufacture and sell drugs for criminal use, lest they be implicated. According to the above methods, if everyone is of one heart and officials and the people cooperate, smugglers and illegal sellers will have no means to practice their tricks.

3. Establish More Smoking Cessation Hospitals and Universally Provide Treatment: This city, with its dense population, is prone to harboring dirt and filth. The people are accustomed to luxury and indulging in pleasure. Therefore, those who indulge in opium are everywhere, mostly poor people. In the 24th year of the Republic, 30,833 smokers were registered in this city, of which 17,995 people applied for poor people's licenses, exceeding the number of ordinary license holders by more than five thousand. These poor people usually earn so little from their labor that it is not enough to support their lives. Once addicted to opium, they have no extra strength to quit on their own. Therefore, it is necessary to establish more smoking cessation hospitals to provide free treatment to smokers and guide them on the path to renewal. This city currently has four smoking cessation hospitals with more than 550 beds, but the number of people who can quit each month is only seven or eight hundred. Except for the two hospitals in South Shanghai and North Shanghai, which fully accommodate smokers who voluntarily seek treatment, the temporary drug rehabilitation centers and the attached criminal smoking cessation hospitals are used for the rehabilitation of smokers caught by the year and special districts. However, the number of beds is limited, and there are many criminals, so it is often impossible to provide universal treatment. To increase the efficiency of smoking cessation, it seems necessary to increase the number of smoking cessation hospitals in this city as much as possible. We should cooperate and discuss with the Health Bureau, the tobacco prohibition agencies in this city, and the courts at all levels in the special district, hoping to promote its realization in the shortest possible time.

4. Build Smoker Factories to Improve Smokers' Environment: The harm of opium is enough to injure people's bodies and erode their will. After most smokers become addicted, their careers are ruined, they cannot produce, and they degenerate to the lower classes, unable to recover. After quitting, they relapse due to unstable lives or environmental temptations. Even severe punishment is not a fundamental solution. It is urgent to raise funds to build large-scale smoker factories to accommodate quitters and criminals who have been sentenced and have served their time. All should be taught skills, their minds and bodies confined, and their physiques tempered, so that when the apprenticeship is completed, their laziness is completely eradicated and they become healthy and productive citizens. This is not only beneficial to the promotion of prohibition but also closely related to social security.

The tobacco prohibition issue is complex. The above four points are only a brief overview of the major issues in this city's social situation. We should know that if tobacco poison is not eliminated for one day, the nation will not prosper for one day, and the great cause of restoration will be difficult to achieve for one day. A journey of a thousand miles begins with a single step. Entrusting a great task to the difficult is our responsibility. I am willing to encourage each other with the people of this city!

China's Tobacco Prohibition and the International Community 160

— Wu Kaixian

The tobacco prohibition movement was originally just a domestic political movement, but in China, it has also become an international movement. The Opium War of 1839 was because China wanted to prohibit opium. The war failed, and under the threat of British guns and cannons, the Chinese government suspended the tobacco prohibition movement. Now, the ugly act of using guns and cannons to interfere with China's tobacco prohibition has not happened again, but the act of using special powers in the treaty to undermine and obstruct China's tobacco prohibition movement still exists. Director-General Chiang Kai-shek of the Anti-Opium Bureau once said painfully, "China's situation in all aspects is relatively special. If the tobacco prohibition matter relies solely on the efforts of the government, it is indeed not easy to achieve thoroughly, because there are many places (especially the concessions in Shanghai, Hankou, and Tianjin), and many malpractices (especially foreigners selling drugs in Chinese territory) that the government's power cannot fully reach." This is a very painful thing. On the one hand, we are distressed that there are places within our territory that our government's power cannot reach. On the other hand, we are even more distressed that such a self-evident matter as the tobacco prohibition movement cannot yet obtain consistent sympathy and assistance from the international community in this era.

A few days ago, the International League of Nations Opium Prohibition Committee held a meeting in Geneva. British and American representatives reported that the Japanese government did not take appropriate and effective measures and questioned them. The Japanese representative did not refute it, only saying that "the Japanese authorities do not fully understand everything" and that "the Japanese government has not condoned drug traffickers." It can be seen that the reports of the British and American representatives are quite reliable. This is not only detrimental to China but also greatly affects the world's tobacco prohibition movement.

After reporting on China's tobacco prohibition plan, Chinese representative Hu Shize said, "In 1935, a total of 970 people were executed for illegally selling, smoking, and manufacturing drugs... The life of the country now depends on the struggle against drugs, which we must persevere to the end." Indeed, the prohibition of tobacco poison has become a prerequisite for our nation's revival. We must thoroughly fight against tobacco poison and eradicate its roots according to the tobacco prohibition plan. We hope that the Japanese government will sympathize with us and take effective measures against its people who sell tobacco poison. China's tobacco prohibition movement will naturally benefit greatly, and the honor of the Japanese Empire in the international community will not be tainted, which will greatly help the harmony of national feelings between China and Japan.

Commemorating "June 3rd" and Our Responsibility 161

— Lu Jingshi

The history of China in the past hundred years can be said to be a dark period of conquest by imperialism. The Opium War was the beginning of this period and the root cause of China's poverty and national weakness.

During the Qianlong and Jiaqing periods of the Qing Dynasty, a large amount of opium was imported annually, and its harmful effects deepened. Although the government had laws prohibiting it, the corruption of officials and the lack of effective enforcement only increased the amount of opium. By the Daoguang period, the government was determined to prohibit it, and the proposals of Lin Zexu, the Governor-General of Guangdong and Guangxi at the time, were the most resolute and thorough. His memorial included several of the most vigilant words: "The poison of opium is worse than floods and fierce beasts. There is no one in the world who thinks opium should not be prohibited. If this disaster is not eliminated, there will be no usable soldiers or funds to raise in ten years." He also ordered Guangdong merchants to hand over the opium, and the British merchants initially refused to comply. After troops were sent to surround the business halls, all the drugs were handed over, totaling 20,283 boxes of opium, worth 560,000 taels of silver, which were all burned at Humen. The news spread, and the whole country cheered.

The British merchants, suffering this blow, used this as an excuse to send troops to attack Guangdong. Our side was prepared and did not succeed. They changed their attack to Dinghai, Ningbo, Zhejiang, and attacked Tianjin to the north. The Qing court was greatly shocked. The general ministers did not understand the situation and, instead of planning resistance, dismissed Lin from his post and sent him to Yili, and then agreed to peace with Britain, signing the Treaty of Nanjing, which was humiliating and harmful to the world. This heroic anti-drug war broke out on "June 3rd." Although the result was such a tragic defeat, this defeat was glorious. Because of our painful sacrifice, the whole world recognized our great national character of not hesitating to pay the highest price to seek the right to survival.

Now it has been ninety-seven years since the Opium War. Looking back, not only has the atmosphere of drugs not been completely eliminated, but the flames of drugs are spreading daily. According to customs statistics, from 1876 to 1928, in these 53 years, the import value of opium was 130 million taels of silver, and the amount secretly smuggled in, which was beyond the customs' knowledge, is even more unknown. Such a huge amount of wasteful consumption, how could the country not be poor? In such an environment, when we commemorate this great and tragic "June 3rd," we have infinite pain and feel the great responsibility we have.

From the historical facts of the Opium War, we have learned a great lesson, that a government without determination cannot accomplish an extraordinary undertaking, especially the complex and serious mission of drug prohibition. The ineffectiveness of drug prohibition in the past ninety years is entirely due to this reason. Now the government knows that the past "taxation on prohibition" is not a solution, so it has made the greatest determination and decided on a two-year drug prohibition and a six-year tobacco prohibition plan, promulgating strict laws and strictly enforcing them. However, "laws alone are not enough to enforce themselves," because laws themselves do not generate power and completely rely on the people to abide by and implement them. The efforts of the government alone cannot complete this great mission. Lin Zexu's failure to prohibit opium in the past was because he lacked loyal comrades and did not have group action. Everything relied on one person's spirit, resulting in failure. Therefore, if we want to seek national liberation and break free from the shackles of imperialist chains, the whole nation should be mobilized to jointly eliminate drugs, supervise the government, and support the government in promoting drug prohibition laws. At the same time, we must supervise, encourage, and advise each other to eliminate the atmosphere of drugs so that China can achieve true liberation. This is our reflection and effort in commemorating "June 3rd" today.

Eliminate Tobacco Poison 162

— Du Yuesheng

The origin of opium is very early. In the Zhenyuan era of the Tang Dynasty (around 800 AD), Arab merchants had already imported the poppy into China. By the middle of the Ming Dynasty (end of the 15th century), the Portuguese monopolized trade in the East. One of their goods, opium, was also called Afuyong in Chinese, which is a transliteration of the Arabic word "Afion." However, opium was initially used as a medicine to treat dysentery, which can be seen in our country's medical books. It was not expected that its accumulation over time would become a habit. Once not smoked, it would be like a sudden onset of a major illness, even more painful than not eating millet. It also damages the spirit and depletes the body, eventually leading to chronic diseases, and the children born will all become weak. Its harm is equal to that of poisonous drugs, harming oneself, harming others, harming society, harming the country, and harming the nation. Therefore, if this disaster is not eliminated, it is undoubtedly certain that all human beings in the world will be poisoned and overthrown, so we must not be afraid.

Our country suffered this poison, and the originators were indeed the Portuguese. However, in the forty-sixth year of Qianlong in the Qing Dynasty (1781), the British East India Company obtained the exclusive right to trade with China from its own government. The Bengal region of India was also a production area of opium. Therefore, it was easier to import into China, and the quantity also increased day by day. Throughout the Qianlong and Jiaqing periods, strict prohibition laws were established, but when the laws were slightly relaxed, traffickers and smokers would return to their old ways. From the twenty-second year of Jiaqing to the eighteenth year of Daoguang, the increase in imports was almost nine times in more than twenty years. The prevalence of opium imports not only caused various evils in the health and morals of the people but also had a great impact on the social economy. The Qing court was worried about this and considered how to deal with the opium problem. Therefore, the prohibition of opium has become the only urgent problem in politics.

On the twenty-ninth day of the first month of the nineteenth year of Daoguang, our memorialized sage Lin Zexu arrived in Guangdong to investigate opium. Based on his indomitable spirit, he developed a plan to eliminate the poison completely. The following year (1840), the Opium War broke out. British troops repeatedly captured important coastal passes and advanced on Nanjing. The Qing court then sent Guangzhou General Qiying and others of the imperial clan to the British warships to discuss the conditions for peace. On August 29, 1842, the envoys of the two countries formally signed the thirteen articles of the Treaty of Jiangning.

Today, after our pain has settled, we should have the greatest awareness of this national "Tobacco Prohibition Day" to eliminate this poisonous substance that destroys the foundation of the country so that we will not fail the teachings of Lin Zexu to us.

Now, our country's government has decided on a comprehensive tobacco prohibition plan, with the momentum to destroy it as if eating breakfast. Our Chairman Chiang, who is also the Director-General of Tobacco Prohibition, has the greatest determination to oversee all matters related to tobacco and drug prohibition throughout the country. In this regard, the people of the country should uphold the government's intentions and assist indirectly and directly to achieve the success of the tobacco prohibition plan and seek the revival of the country and the nation. In this dangerous national situation, we have no other way to follow than self-reliance. The harm of opium, harming the country and stupefying the people, is known to everyone. Its most obvious harm is the damage to the social economy. Why do I say that? Because there are so many smokers, the amount of money spent on smoking is staggering, and its impact on production is unknown! Looking ahead and behind, we cannot help but sigh with emotion. It is hoped that people with lofty ideals and patriotic compatriots will rise up to eliminate it.
