Education News

Ministry of Education Eliminates Illiteracy Nationwide – Drafts Measures to Promote People's Education 163

(Nanjing, 2nd) The Ministry of Education considers eliminating illiteracy nationwide to be the most pressing task at present. It is now planning to completely eliminate the 200 million illiterate people within six years. The responsible department is currently drafting measures to promote people's education, which will be implemented after being approved by the Executive Yuan.

Number and Major of National Higher Education Graduates in Recent Four Years 164

The Ministry of Education compiled statistics on the number and major of graduates from national colleges and universities in the recent four years in May of this year. The following is a summary:

(Explanation) In terms of numbers, in the 20th year of the Republic, among the 7,034 people, 5,428 were undergraduates (universities and colleges), and 1,606 were vocational students (vocational schools and university colleges). In the 21st year of the Republic, among the 7,311 people, 5,515 were undergraduates, and 1,756 were vocational students. In the 22nd year of the Republic, among the 8,665 people, 6,790 were undergraduates, and 1,915 were vocational students. In the 23rd year of the Republic, among the 9,626 people, 8,329 were undergraduates, and 1,297 were vocational students. In terms of major, practical subjects accounted for 26.77% in the 20th year of the Republic, 27.59% in the 21st year, 29.57% in the 22nd year, and 28.67% in the 23rd year. Liberal arts subjects accounted for 73.23% in the 20th year, 72.41% in the 21st year, 70.43% in the 22nd year, and 71.33% in the 23rd year. Generally speaking, the number of higher education graduates has increased year by year in the recent four years, and the number of science graduates in the 23rd year is more than double that of the 20th year, and engineering has increased by 120%, which is quite in line with the needs of the times. However, the Ministry of Education has slightly restricted the increase in liberal arts graduates, and it may be reduced in the future.

Staff meeting held yesterday. Good weather, decision to open on the 6th

The 7th convention, grand review, and camping of the City Boy Scouts is scheduled to open on June 6th. Location: Central area of Shanghai City. 3. Funding: Allocated by the city treasury. 4. Preparation: The Shanghai Special City Council of the Boy Scouts of China hires several organizing committee members to be responsible for preparation. 5. Souvenirs: All troop departments participating in the convention will be given souvenirs and certificates. Service personnel and Boy Scouts will be given souvenir badges.

Hubei Province's Free Education and Special Education 170

Limited Funding, Vigorous Promotion: Mr. Cheng Chizhi, Director of Education in Hubei Province, attended the meeting of department heads and commissioners convened by the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Education's special education conference for five provinces. He arrived in Beijing yesterday. A reporter visited him, intending to inquire about the province's education situation. Seeing that Mr. Cheng had just finished his journey and was busy with visitors, the reporter only asked about the situation of compulsory education and special education. He replied, and a brief summary is as follows: The province of Hubei promotes compulsory education with funding of 270,000 yuan, of which 130,000 yuan is provided by the central government through subsidies from the Ministry of Education, and 140,000 yuan is raised by the province. Although the funding is limited, it has been able to realize the plan. Recently, 900 new elementary schools have been promoted. As for compulsory education in various counties, it was originally planned that each county would add more than 5,000 Lianbao elementary schools (thousands of existing schools were outside), which would cost more than one million yuan. Due to natural and man-made disasters, it has been slightly affected. The provincial department is working hard to supervise and promote it. Now, more than 3,000 Lianbao elementary schools have been added in various counties, and the original plan will be achieved soon. The special education funding in Hubei Province is only 80,000 yuan per year, which is used for leadership and experimental work. The Zhongshan People's Schools in various counties are used as units for promotion. The teachers of the People's Schools assist the local government in promoting education, cultivation, and health work, divided into three types of classes: children, adults, and women. There are more children's classes. Currently, more than 100 classes have been established in various counties, which is quite effective. In addition, civic training classes are also held. In addition to teaching required courses, they also provide group life training. Each term lasts four months, and the third term has been completed.

Fourth Term of Municipal Literacy School Examination in This City 175

Heard That the Fifth Term is Scheduled to Start in July

The fourth term of the municipal literacy school in this city has been in session since March 1st. Now that the three-month term is over, the municipal government sent personnel to various schools to conduct examinations in the past two days. It is heard that since the municipal government implemented compulsory literacy education in July last year, the original plan was to eliminate all illiteracy in the urban area within one year. However, the period of literacy school was extended to three months, and only four terms were held in one year. Therefore, the number of graduates only accounts for half of the total number of illiterate people. Although this year is coming to an end, in order to thoroughly eliminate illiteracy, it has been decided to continue to hold it in the next year. However, the implementation method may be changed. Literacy school teachers still need to be trained intensively. The period for the start of the fifth term is probably in mid-July.

Children's Literature and Art Society Publishes "From Elementary School to Junior High School" 176

Special Price for Sale During the Painting Exhibition

In order to celebrate the National Children's Painting Exhibition, the Chinese Children's Literature and Art Society specially compiled and printed the book "From Elementary School to Junior High School". The children participating in this painting exhibition are all elementary and junior high school students. The content of the book starts with the differences between elementary and junior high schools, and then discusses how to develop healthy junior high school students, and then discusses the basic principles of junior high school students' studies. Then, it discusses the learning methods of various subjects in junior high school. The content is rich and appropriate, and the writing is concise. It is a good reference book for elementary school graduates and junior high school students. It is inscribed by Minister Wang of the Ministry of Education and prefaced by Director Pan of the Municipal Education Bureau. The content is signed and titled by the directors of the education departments of various provinces and cities across the country and the presidents of famous primary and secondary schools. The pattern expert Zhou Xibao also specially painted the cover with profound meaning. The entire book has been printed earlier, with more than 80,000 words and more than 100 pages. In order to commemorate the book exhibition, it is scheduled to be sold on June 6th. In addition to giving 1,000 copies as prizes, the book price will be reduced by 20% to 84 cents. Postage will not be added separately. The company will also produce 10,000 commemorative badges for the book exhibition, and each book will be given one badge, but it is limited to being given away during the exhibition period. Readers from outside the area can order directly from the special distributor of the society at No. 361 Penglai Road, Shanghai, the China Art Company, and postage stamps below 5 cents are also fully accepted.

Sports News

China-France Davis Cup Match Report 180

— Zhou Nianxian

The French Have a Very Good Impression of Zheng Zhaojia and Lin Baohua

(Paris Correspondence) I am very fond of tennis. Considering the domestic enthusiasts, I would like to inform the Chinese people about the Sino-French battle in the Davis Cup. Of course, you all know the result of the score. What is described here is a more detailed record and comments from all parties. My selfless criticism is also frankly stated below.

On the afternoon of May 1st, under cloudy skies and in a gentle breeze, the Sino-French Davis Cup match began. In the first singles match, Xu Chengji faced Boossus. Under a non-tense situation, he sent two sets in a row, creating a rare record with 6-0, 6-0. In the third set, he stayed a bit on the surface and ended the game with 6-1. The French newspaper said that the competition failed to show Boossus's skills and there was nothing to describe. However, I want to remind readers of a few points. Mr. Boossus is a world-renowned player with many years of experience. No player in our country can be his opponent. In addition, Mr. Xu is not physically strong, and he was also affected by the wind and waves on the 25th. The field was unfamiliar and the climate was unaccustomed. The truth is excusable. However, the audience cannot understand it, Mr. Xu's movements are too slow, he is unwilling to do his best, he only seeks to parry, and does not seek to make progress. Thinking back to Mr. Xu's success in China, it is really puzzling. Or it is predicted that his physical condition is not good, and I think that is the reason. In the second game, the situation of Zheng Zhaojia against Destremau was completely changed. Zheng immediately scored a game when he came on the court. When the opponent saw that the situation was not right, he cautiously responded to the enemy, and took both offense and defense. He finally won the first set 6-1. After this set of confrontation, Mr. Zheng got the hang of it, and his skills were also more novel. He eventually lost the second set with 3-6. The third set gradually improved. He took the lead with 2-1 at the beginning. Encouraged by more than 100 compatriots, he was full of energy and worked hard to fight. Blood reached 4 times 2, and then became a draw. Mr. Te regained the victory with a serve, and became 5-6. Although the French side had a superior situation, their energy was exhausted. Mr. Zheng's balls were calm, such as winning three consecutive serves, resulting in a 6-6 tie. He won the third set with 8-6 after repeatedly winning with backhand heavy shots. After a ten-minute break, the fourth set began. Mr. Zheng took the lead again with 2-0. The opponent was terrified and gave up offense in favor of defense. Mr. Zheng's online skills were poor, so he did not win. However, the air was unusually tense. Later, due to fairness, Mr. Zheng lost consecutively and became 2-3. Then from 3 to 3 to 3-6, and lost the fourth set.

The competition on the first day ended. The French newspaper gave a very good evaluation of Mr. Zheng. It admired his brave spirit, and believed that his strength should be above Mr. Xu, and allowed him to be listed at the end of the world's first-class players.

On the second day, the weather was clear and sunny. Xu Chengji and Lin Shihua took the stage to face the enemy and competed with the French Borotra and Benrand. Although Mr. Xu was active, he still lacked highlights, while Lin Shihua won a lot of applause with his shots and online skills. The upper hand is always unfamiliar, and the first set failed 6-1. However, due to the two gentlemen's loyalty and courage, the second set was created from 1-3 to a 3-3 tie. The French side saw that the situation was tense, and Borotra showed off his skills, and eventually lost the second set with 1-6. According to convention, the turning point is often in the third set. Looking at our side's victory, the French side borrowed the remaining prestige of the victory and took the lead with 2-0. However, after Ba's serve, it was repeatedly unfavorable, and it became a 2-1. Xu Chengji's shots this time were unusually successful. After five engagements, it became a 3-2 tie. After several hard-fought battles, our side took the lead with 4-3. After that, both sides often went online, and the excitement was unusual. Our enemy each got one game, resulting in a 5-4 advantage. When it was Lin Shihua's turn to serve, he hit hard with his arm, and the ball was close to the line. The opponent had difficulty returning the ball, and our army won three consecutive balls, and then won the third set with 6-4 with Lin's clever net blocking. After a 15-minute break, he went on stage again. Mr. Xu often made mistakes, causing the enemy to take the lead with 3-0. When it was Mr. Xu's turn to hit the ball, Mr. Xu cheered up to fight and won two consecutive games, resulting in a ratio of 2 to 3. Then Benrand's net blocking was effective, and he made beautiful moves from time to time. Our side was defeated with 1-1 due to poor contact. After these three games, our country has been eliminated. But the two singles on the third day continued. That night, the newspapers also praised Lin for his playing, but regretted that the two had poor contact. The result of the game on the third day was predictable. However, the most noteworthy thing was the game between Zheng Zhaojia and Boossus. In the fourth game, Xu Chengji first played against Destremau. Because Mr. Xu saw that the opponent was weaker, he was slightly bolder, so he attacked more. It was a pity that it was still too late, so he lost the first two sets with 3-6 and 2-6. However, his steady cross-corner shots were really skillful and should not be buried. Therefore, he often used good moves and won the third set with 6-4. After resting for ten minutes according to regulations, he fought again with a spiritual mind. The French side knew that Mr. Te's strength was weak and feared failure, so he cared for and loved him and helped him especially. It was a pity that Mr. Xu was defeated with 2-6. However, to be fair, Mr. Te is only eighteen and a half years old and is participating in the Davis Cup for the first time this year. I hope Mr. Xu will work hard to make progress and comfort the public's expectations.

After Mr. Xu finished the game, Mr. Zheng played against Boossus. The result was not outstanding. The score was 6-0, 6-0, 6-0, which was similar to Mr. Xu's. But his efforts in the game and his courage to chase the ball were really admirable. Mr. Pu's game against Zheng was no longer as easy as against Xu, and he sometimes felt difficult to deal with. Looking at the number of balls returned in the first set, you can see that there was a fierce battle. Mr. Zheng's shots against Mr. Pu mostly went to his left hand at first. This is the usual tactic. However, when the enemy uses his left hand, the strategy should be changed. The main reason for Mr. Zheng's failure in one set was this. In the last two sets, Mr. Zheng changed to shooting at the enemy's right hand, and Mr. Pu had difficulty coping with it. This is why the game in the second set was relatively close. In short, although Mr. Zheng and Mr. Xu both lost, the process was more beautiful. The French newspaper never stopped praising his bravery. I also wish Mr. Zheng hard work and unlimited future.

Shen Bao National Products Special Issue

Contribution Talk

Industrial Inventors 206

— Yang An

Invention is a good sign of progress in industry. What our people lack most is the ability to invent things. Therefore, Mr. Zhang Boling once said, "Europeans and Americans create, Japanese imitate, and Chinese do nothing." This is such a shameful thing. However, recently I feel that the interest of Chinese people in inventing things is becoming stronger day by day. Last year, according to statistics, there were thirty-eight cases of inventions by Chinese people that were submitted to the Ministry of Industry for patent and exclusive rights. It is unknown how much brainpower and effort was spent, how much measurement was used, and how many difficulties were overcome to achieve such a small accomplishment. These admirable inventors are the treasures of the country, the glory of the Chinese nation, and especially the most honorable page in the history of Chinese industry.

Recently, I visited three factories: one is the pressure vegetable oil lamp invented by Mr. Zhong Ling of the China Oil Lamp Factory, one is the month, day, week, hour clock invented by Mr. Ruan Shunfa of the China Educational Toy Factory, and the other is the free five-use light bulb invented by Mr. Bao Yimin of the Qite Free Light Bulb Factory. After my visit, I felt that these three kinds of appliances are all necessities for daily life. Vegetable oil lamps can make better use of domestic vegetable oil, laying the foundation for national self-sufficiency, and their effect is especially great. What is most commendable is that Ruan Shunfa came from a shipyard worker background, and Bao Yimin is a worker at a power company. They already have a deep understanding, and they are able to painstakingly study things, work hard on research, spend three or four years of effort, painstakingly and tirelessly, to achieve such accomplishments. I am very admirable. And I express that following the efforts of Ruan and Bao, China's future will definitely be very promising. I think that the number of college graduates in China year after year is no less than several thousand, all complaining that there is nothing to do, no occupation, and no opportunity to develop their talents. But I have searched through the inventors and found that very few are college students. Where is the contribution of college students? Reflecting on oneself, one can only be speechless. And Ruan and Bao were able to create things as workers and make this kind of contribution. Moreover, among the inventors, none have received advanced education. We are very ashamed, and I think many college students should be ashamed. Therefore, I think that the government should give as much encouragement, support, and assistance to inventors as possible in the future, so that there will be more and more inventors in the future, and China's industry will have hope for regeneration.

My Views on National Goods Awards 207

— Li Boshu

The prosperity of a country is, in any case, directly proportional to the development of its industry and commerce. When a country's domestic goods industry develops, naturally, foreign goods will have no way to invade, or at least they will not be able to stand firm in the country. Therefore, enabling the domestic goods industry to develop to the greatest extent is the fundamental, thorough, and proactive way to revive the national economy. Of course, in our external relations, we should resolutely resist the invasion of foreign goods; and internally, we should only strive for the development of the domestic goods industry. This is as practical and effective as a person striving to strengthen their own physical strength to resist the invasion of external germs.

Then, to seek the development of the domestic goods industry, on the one hand, we must work hard to promote it, but the government must also have an expression of encouragement, so that the domestic goods industry can fully manufacture more perfect products, so that the public can truly enjoy using them. This way, we can give foreign goods a strong blow. Therefore, I believe that national goods awards are indeed necessary. This key can indeed affect the prosperity of the national economy.

Secondly, what I want to explain is that the so-called national goods awards are completely different from patent rights, etc. Although their nature is the same in terms of encouragement, the methods are completely different. In my opinion, this fund should be raised by the Ministry of Industry in advance, and a large-scale (national) national goods exhibition should be held every year. People should be sent by the government to evaluate them on the spot (of course, this work is very difficult, but as long as more people are sent to criticize, at least some subjectivity can be avoided). The top-quality products should be selected and recorded in detail, and the award money should be distributed to the producers separately. In this way, not only can it create a kind of fierce competition in the national goods industry, but it can also give everyone in the national goods industry the opportunity to observe.

Finally, I also hope that the domestic goods industry will conduct joint discussions.

The Anti-Smoking Day and the Promotion of National Medicine 208

— Ba Ling

Today, June 3rd, is the National Anti-Smoking and Anti-Drug Day designated by the National Government. All parts of the country are enthusiastically carrying out anti-smoking and anti-drug propaganda, which is indeed a very meaningful and valuable work. From the standpoint of revitalizing the nation, it is especially felt to be a matter of urgency.

However, in my opinion, anti-drug and anti-smoking propaganda is of course very important and urgent. During the Qing Dynasty, Mr. Lin Zexu, who strongly advocated strictly prohibiting opium, once said: "If China does not strictly prohibit opium, then in ten years, not only will there be no usable soldiers, but there will also be no funds to raise..." Mr. Sun Yat-sen, the leader of the Chinese Kuomintang, also said: "Any revolutionary government vows not to compromise with opium drugs!" It is already very clear that opium should be strictly prohibited, and there is no need to say more here! However, on the one hand, we should certainly support the government's efforts to implement the anti-smoking plan. At the same time, on the other hand, we should also work hard to promote the national medicine movement. That is the right thing to do.

Why do we want to shout out the slogan of promoting the national medicine movement on the Anti-Smoking Day today? We know that most of the gentlemen are addicted to opium because they gradually became addicted when they were sick and wanted to treat their illnesses. After becoming addicted, they cannot help but smoke every day, so they are always drunk beside the opium bed, wasting time, losing their jobs, and losing their family fortunes. All of this is due to the initial carelessness, which leads to a tragic ending.

Our promotion of the national medicine movement is to ensure that people in general, when they are sick, must not approach opium, and must not have the idea that smoking opium will cure their ailments. It must be known that opium is a kind of poison that kills without bloodshed. Anyone who comes into contact with it will be harmed by it. Moreover, among the national medicines, there are many medicines that are far superior to opium, and will never be addictive after taking them. Today, when the national anti-smoking day is held, the author has specially put forward the slogan of promoting the national medicine movement, which may not be a meaningless thing.

Review of the Use of Domestic Raw Materials for Civil Servants' Uniforms 209

— Zhu Qin

The Central Government recently instructed all national party departments, agencies, groups, schools, etc., to wear formal attire when holding the Premier's Memorial Week. Men: black mandarin jacket and blue robe or Zhongshan suit; women: long jacket or shirt and skirt. Must be clean and simple, and the color should be suitable for the season. Uniform raw materials should all use domestic goods. Due to the point that the uniforms use domestic raw materials, we have to have a review of the necessity of this.

Civil servants are models for the public and must lead the masses by setting an example in everything. This time, the Central Government instructed that civil servants' uniforms must use domestic goods. As a matter of course, we do not need these four words "use domestic goods" to be notified. In fact, the minds of Chinese people have become everywhere subject to the restraint of others and cannot grasp their own initiative to do things. Therefore, the uniforms of civil servants, who are models for the people, must also add the order of the four words "use domestic goods."

When we see ordinary civil servants, including leaders of party, government, military, and police agencies, and middle and senior officials, and use sharp eyes to estimate the clothing on their bodies, speaking from our own conscience, how many use pure domestic silk and cloth to make uniforms? They not only make expensive imported fabrics into neat Western suits and Zhongshan suits, but also cannot find anything on their bodies made of domestic raw materials. They take care of all their own "foreign goods" and shout the slogan of promoting "domestic goods," whether in gatherings, speeches, or between the lines, are not they encouraging the public to use "domestic goods" together? This is simply the extreme of contradiction, which invisibly loses the people's faith in using domestic goods.

Indeed, "leading by example" is not an easy thing. Empty talk and high-sounding slogans are things that everyone can do. Anyway, doing it in a practical and realistic way must be done with perseverance and determination.

So I earnestly hope that the authorities will seriously consider the issue of "using domestic goods" for civil servants' uniforms. I think there are the following two ways to make civil servants' uniforms use pure domestic raw materials:

The government designates pure raw materials made of domestic silk or cotton fabrics produced by domestic goods manufacturers, and orders party, government, military, police agencies, groups, schools, etc. in various provinces and cities to uniformly use the clothing materials produced by the factory to make uniforms. The clothing material colors must be in season, and the government determines the purchase and manufacture, and the styles must be consistent to achieve the goal of economic simplicity, beauty and neatness.

Civilian officials must wear black mandarin jackets and blue robes, which has been clearly ordered, but the black mandarin jackets and blue robes must be limited to the use of domestic cloth or silk, and imported clothing materials must not be purchased. The same applies to military officer uniforms, ordering party, government, military, police agencies, groups, schools, etc. in various provinces and cities to uniformly obey, and formulate reward and punishment measures for civil servants using domestic goods, and commend or admonish based on whether civil servants use domestic goods or not. This measure must be supervised and implemented by the highest officials, and can be included in the performance appraisal measures for civil servants.

The former of the above two points can give domestic goods the opportunity to be sold to civil servants and national agencies throughout the country, and can enable domestic goods manufacturers to have the convenience of developing the domestic apparel industry, and can also reduce the amount of dumping of imported goods. The latter can enable civil servants to stop buying imported goods, blocking loopholes. This will not only expand the sales force of domestic goods in the future, but also block the dykes from our country's economic and financial resources flowing abroad. I also hope that the government authorities, domestic goods manufacturers, and fellow students will jointly review it.

Technique 212

— Zhu Ying

Technique is a basic quality of art. If art lacks technique, it cannot be art. For example, in the narration of a very ordinary story, those who are good at art can use very ordinary words to narrate it in a way that makes people laugh, cry, get excited, or even sympathize, so that any reader, when reading this story, seems to be experiencing it personally, witnessing everything, or even feeling like they have become one of the protagonists in the story, so closely related to their pain and joy. This is the narrator's skill in using his narrative techniques. On the other hand, those who are not good at technique, even though the paper is full of embroidered words that are arranged in pairs and sound harmonious, will ultimately only make the reader feel like they are reading a narrative text of a story.

Painting is also the same. Painters who are skilled in technique can use a few strokes and a simple structure to form a picture that can attract the eyes of the reader and is even more fascinating. Photography is also the same. Only those who can increase the quality and reduce the quantity can include the technical qualities inherent in their art in their products. I once read a notebook by a certain old man and saw a record of a fortune teller. Someone picked the word "fish" to ask about their fortune in life. He saw someone passing by carrying water and said, "Like a fish in water." Another person saw it and also pointed to the word "fish" to ask about good and bad luck. He saw a cat on the opposite house and shook his head, saying, "The mouth of the cat is a disaster." Someone picked the word "pagoda," and he said, "Step by step, you will rise higher." Another person also pointed to this "pagoda" to ask for a fortune, and he said, "The position you are standing in is opposite to the pagoda, so the lower you go, the narrower it becomes - a complete mess." This fortune teller can be said to have won people over with his skill.

Another example is playing cards. Although it is one of the leisurely occupations, card players cannot lack skill. With the same deck of cards, those who are skilled in technique can play a card and wait for three or even four calls. Those who are not skilled in technique will finish after waiting for two calls. Cook Ding always makes dishes with the same flavor, but housewives can make one or two new dishes, showing their unique cooking skills.

Some people say that skill is evolved from experience. I think skill is the crystallization of talent. Therefore, only those who have the talent to be a person can have the skill to deal with the world and gain a position; otherwise, no matter how hard you try, you will always work hard and not be able to please others.

Chatting with Gu Chuanjie About Kun Opera 213

— Xue

Gu Chuanjie, a famous young actor of Kun Opera who was extremely praised by the general public in Shanghai seven or eight years ago, is no longer living the life on the red carpet. We can find him at Jinling University in the capital, and, strangely enough, he is not only not studying in the drama department, but he is not in the liberal arts at all, but in agricultural science. According to several of our friends who are relatively close to him, he does have the ambition to go to the countryside and work hard.

Half a month ago, I met him again at the clinic of my old friend Dr. Chen Cunren. He did not come from Nanjing to see a doctor on purpose. In fact, there was another reason; this reason cannot be revealed temporarily, but it is roughly related to Mr. Xiong Shiyi's production of the play "Romance of the West Chamber" in the UK and the US.

We chatted casually for a while and unknowingly talked about Kun Opera again. Kun Opera has become an abandoned art form in the current art scene. What is the reason for this? According to Gu Chuanjie's criticism:

There is no organized promotion and advocacy;

Kun Opera practitioners and general amateurs are too old-fashioned in their thinking and do not know how to be progressive.

These three points are indeed the fatal flaws of Kun Opera. Even I often feel that Kun Opera is actually not difficult and is very interesting, but why can't it occupy a considerable position in the theater world? It is truly an incredible strange thing. After we discussed with Mr. Gu Chuanjie again and again that day, we both believed that Kun Opera does have the need to be preserved and promoted. First of all, everyone should change the saying of "too sophisticated to be popular," and know that although the lyrics of Kunqu Opera are more profound, the performers always sing and act at the same time. The audience does not need to fully understand its lyrics, and they can get an idea of it from the actors' expressions; moreover, the dialogues in Kun Opera are extremely clear and easy to understand, and are no different from Peking Opera. Mr. Gu believes that if efforts can be made in the following points in the future: distributing brochures during performances, paying attention to improving the scenery and props, and training new talents, then it will not be a difficult task to revive Kun Opera.

Mr. Gu also believes that in the eyes of Europeans and Americans, Kun Opera is more welcome than Peking Opera, but when Mr. Mei Lanfang performed several plays when he went abroad, "Assassinating the Tiger" was indeed the most highly praised, which is a clear proof.

Interesting Talk about Hall Names 214

— Lan Shan

In the past, those who loved elegance and culture, whenever they built a room or set up a store, would always ask famous public figures to write plaques for them, considering it an honor. Therefore, there were many kinds of names such as pavilions, buildings, halls, rooms, residences, gardens, huts, pavilions, houses, studios, and inns, which were too numerous to count. If the plaques were well-written, there were certainly not a few of them in ancient and modern times. Now, let's just talk about a few interesting ones:

Someone wrote a plaque for a mediocre doctor's hall, calling it "Mingyuan Hall." When asked why, he replied: "Haven't you read the Analects? It says: '...not acting is called clarity...not acting is called distance.' In this way, 'Mingyuan' means not acting, not acting."

Also, a servant became rich and built a large residence, asking a celebrity to write a plaque, which was written with the three characters "Danbai Hall." When asked about the meaning, he said: "A young actress always calls herself a slave. The meaning of 'Danbai' comes from this (seen in Xiaolin)."

There was also someone who named a tavern "Zhe Zhe Ju," telling people, "I take the meaning of pleasing those who are near and attracting those who are far away." It can be said that it has a special idea.

One person started his career as a blacksmith, and his brother was a tanner. After getting rich, each built a residence, asking celebrities to write plaques to hide their humble origins. A celebrity wrote a plaque for his brother, saying "Eryou Hall;" and a plaque for his younger brother, saying "Jiayi Hall." The two were overjoyed and hung them in the middle hall. Little did they know that looking at "Eryou" directly, it looked like the anvil used by blacksmiths; looking at "Eryou" horizontally, it was like bellows. As for the character "Jia," it looked like the steel cone used by tanners, and the character "Yi" looked like a leather knife. They all used pictographic words to fool these brothers (also seen in Xiaolin).

Swapping the Nests of Luan and Phoenix 215

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Two: Fragrant Grass and Beautiful Women Trust to the Waves / Moonlight Night in a Small Building, Good Dreams are Just Beginning

Speaking of this girl, she kept turning her head back. Was she really looking at people? But she made it clear that she had other feelings. She sighed and said to her sister-in-law: There are a lot of wild graves in the mountains, I'm afraid the buried people aren't the right kind. If I die, I will entrust the two of you, my sisters-in-law, to bury me here. Maybe I can be worthy of this piece of land. An older young woman laughed: Menglan, why are you always saying such depressing things these days? Menglan said: It's not depressing at all. Everyone dies once, and can they avoid being buried in the ground after death? This Yuhuatai buried Fang Xiaoru, a great loyal minister of the Ming Dynasty. If we die, burying us next to the grave of a great loyal minister is also a great honor. A younger young woman said: That's true, but if you really have that day, it will be when you are seventy or eighty years old, with children and grandchildren all around, and then we will carry you up the mountain. Menglan immediately walked faster and left them, covering her ears with both hands. The two young women behind her laughed and followed, constantly calling out: Walk slower! We won't say anything about you anymore. After getting off the mountain, Menglan's sorrow did not diminish, making the two sisters-in-law inconvenient to say anything more. Fortunately, she was always worried, so the two sisters-in-law didn't mind. It turned out that this Miss Menglan's surname was Jiang, and she was the daughter of a wealthy family in this city. She was eighteen years old this year and was studying at Zhenkun Girls' Middle School in the west of the city. Today is Sunday, and something unspeakable happened at home. Her mother, Mrs. Jiang, said to her two daughters-in-law that the weather was very good, so take Menglan out to play. Unexpectedly, they ran into Zhang Guoqi again when they went to Yuhuatai, which made her feel even more bitter. After returning home, she didn't say anything and went straight back to the small building where she lived. The houses in Nanjing's mansions have always followed one after another, and can directly connect to seven or eight levels. Menglan's house has a total of six levels. A small building was built on the second level from the end. Behind the building, there is a small courtyard with a rose trellis, two or three trees, seven or eight banana trees, and small potted plants and Taihu stones dotted around, which can be considered a garden. On the right side of the courtyard is a whitewashed wall. Outside the wall, it is close to other people's vegetable gardens. There are two old willow trees that are several decades old, rising high into the air. Menglan sat upstairs, with a desk facing the window, and she always loved to stare at these two tall willows in a daze. This day, when she returned home, she went upstairs, washed her face, and sat down by the desk, wanting to find a book to calm her mind. At this moment, the maid Wu Ma came in with a teapot and a paper roll. When Menglan saw it, her face immediately lit up with a smile, and she took the paper roll in her hand. Then she quickly found a small knife in the oil and slowly and gently peeled open the paper, which was a book with very beautiful characters on it. On the other side were four words, which were "Double Star Magazine." (30)

What I Saw 216

— (Meng Ping)

The night before last, at ten o'clock, I boarded the Route 20 trolleybus parked at Jing'an Temple, wanting to return to Zhaofeng Park. The first-class carriages always have more empty seats, so I bought more first-class tickets. But that night was an exception, the first-class was already full of people, so I went into the third-class carriage, enjoying the two copper coins that were cheaper; moreover, there were only twenty-five people there, with many empty seats. But the first-class customers became more and more numerous, and those who arrived later had to stand. Naturally, their clothes and shoes were well-groomed, and they were undoubtedly people from the middle class and above.

But what is really puzzling is that the eyes of those standing people glanced at us third-class carriage passengers, a mere twenty-five of us, and then quickly retracted them. They didn't care about the many empty seats. Would they rather stand than sit in this cheap carriage with seats? Are they afraid of lowering their status or preventing their clothes and shoes from getting dirty?

Liu Dabai and Double Red Beans 217

— Yu Youqing

Red beans and men of letters, when a relationship occurs, apart from Wang Wei, styled Mojie, of the Tang Dynasty, Qian Qianyi, styled Muqi, of the late Ming Dynasty, and Hui Dong, styled Dingyu, of the early Qing Dynasty, the late poet Liu Dabai can be counted as one.

To speak of the relationship between Dabai and red beans, let's first talk about his life. In the anthology of poems edited by Zhu Ziqing in the "Anthology of New Chinese Literature," there is a passage:

Liu Dabai, named Jingyi, known by his courtesy name, was a native of Shaoxing, Zhejiang. Deceased. He has "Old Dreams" (later re-edited as "Ning's Re-creation: Autumn's Shanghai Cloth-Selling Ballad"), "Postal Kisses." In the self-introduction to the printing of "Old Dreams," it is said: "His new traditional flavor is too strong, and this flavor is recurrently reappearing, not easy to eliminate." It also says: "He uses the pen too heavily, loves to say everything, and has little implication."

At the same time, in the "Elementary Chinese Textbooks for Middle Schools," there is also a passage in the author's short biography:

Liu Dabai (modern), a native of Shaoxing, Zhejiang, successively served as the Director of the Department of Chinese Literature at Fudan University in Shanghai, concurrently as the Director of Shiyan Middle School, Secretary of the Education Department of Zhejiang Province, Secretary-General of the National Zhejiang University, Permanent Vice Minister of the Ministry of Education of the National Government, and Political Vice Minister of the Ministry of Education. He is the author of "Old Dreams," "Postal Kisses," "Liao Ning"

(above are poetry collections), "New Talks on Old Poems," "White House Literary Talks," and other books.

I have written it out verbosely. Furthermore, Mr. Xia Mianzun sent me a "Short History of Chinese Celebrities" (?). Unfortunately, I lost it; otherwise, I could introduce it in more detail and arouse Dabai's interest in red beans. Because Zhou Gangzhi of Jiangyin sent him a pair of red beans (it was New Year's Day in 1924), and not long after, he wrote a prose piece called "Double Red Beans" (published in "New Talks on Old Poems"). In that article, there are three "Double Red Bean" poems, written delicately and touchingly, very lovely. However, after the double red beans, the issue of love arose. He gave the red beans to Wu Fuxia; in other words, he gave his love to Wu Fuxia. But Fuxia was not very passionate about Dabai. The main reason was that Dabai was poor and didn't know how to make money, so Fuxia said, "What I need, you cannot satisfy." This refers to both the economic and, of course, the spiritual aspects. Nevertheless, Dabai's passion increased greatly, which can be glimpsed in "Ode." "Ode" is a new-style poem with four stanzas, each beginning with "Xia is most worthy of being praised." Later, in Hangzhou, a rift developed between the two, which can be roughly seen in "Farewell," like "Spring returns in sickness, people have been apart for a long time, not for lovesickness, but also for lovesickness." "When does the letter arrive, when does the letter arrive?" "Is it a dream, why not, is it a dream, why not try?" It can be known Dabai's pain at that time. Later, Fuxia lived in Xiaoshan, sleeping in the arms of another man, not thinking of the elderly Dabai. When Dabai and Fuxia separated, Dabai was extremely painful. He said, "Tearing up old dreams, determined to tear up old dreams, seems to be constantly on my mind!"

Later, Dabai died. A certain lady went to Hangzhou to mourn and wail at the coffin. Dabai's family and friends did not know who she was. She claimed to have a deep love relationship with Dabai, had lived with him, and produced double red beans as proof. From this perspective, whether that certain lady was Wu Fuxia is still a mystery. If it was really Wu Fuxia, she had some conscience after all, not forgetting her past lover, wailing at the coffin. Unfortunately, the deceased is gone, how would he know that Xia, the one most worthy of his praise, came to mourn? Afterwards, who knows who will possess this pair of red beans?

Dabai was a sentimental person and also a poor scholar. It's a pity that a pair of red beans was entrusted to a woman who disliked poverty. Dabai wrote articles and poems for the sake of the red beans and gave them to his lover. However, his life was too painful.

In my humble compilation "Anthology of Red Beans," I included Dabai's "Double Red Beans" in the "Posthumous Works of Red Beans," and at the same time appended his high-achieving student Cao Juren's "Acacia Seed" and the "Red Beans" from "Metropolitan Scenery" in "Morning Post," so that the poets who have passed away may know something about their lives. Unexpectedly, ten years later, there is a fool who promotes and publishes them!

Acknowledgement: "The Chinese Who's Who" published by Gujin Library Du Fa Xing has been published. The book collects materials with great effort. The content is divided into more than ten categories, such as sages, heroes, generals, civil servants, loyal martyrs, upright men, chivalrous men, strategists, and artists, from the Yellow Emperor Zhou Qin to the end of the Qing Dynasty. There are thousands of celebrities, about one million words. It is indeed a must-have book for reference in all fields. The whole book consists of three thick volumes, the original price is five yuan, and the special price is four yuan. The local stores are at No. 291 Simalu Road, and mail orders can be sent to the company at No. 179 Lane 179 Kang Nao Tu Road. I received a copy yesterday, so I would like to thank you.

Stomach Pain Requires Treatment of the Cause 220

— Zhan Nianceng

The pathology of stomach pain has been detailed in previous issues of this publication. Radical treatment with medicine. There are also many medical examples. Talks

Teachers Starving and Unable to Endure Suicide 228

— Jianping

The education field is a "pure and poor" path, which everyone should admit. "Pure and poor" means that you can still live. At most, you won't get rich, but you won't starve to death. Therefore, many people think that entering the education field is "pure and noble." —— Those people who remember "noble" and forget the "bitter" dream still exist now. Unfortunately, things are not that simple. There are many things in this world that go wrong with people. Take the example of the education field. Now it has fallen to "distress." "Pure" is out of the question, and "living" seems not easy. The intermittent salary-demanding movements of teachers in various places are good iron proof. Perhaps, some people still think that salary-demanding movements are just "accidental" phenomena and do not believe that the bankruptcy of the education field is really like this. Then, please look at the recent tragedy in Xuzhou where teachers ran out of food, were unable to endure starvation, and committed suicide!

A telegram from Tongshan on May 28: Xuzhou education fees are bankrupt, and schools owe salaries for as long as eight months, leaving teachers without food. A teacher at Zuowa Elementary School, unable to endure starvation, suddenly committed suicide, triggering a salary-demanding movement among the entire education community.

The teacher's "sudden suicide" was because of "running out of food" and "unable to endure starvation." And these two reasons are determined by "education fees being bankrupt," which leads to "salaries being owed for eight months." From this, we can understand that this will never be an "accidental" thing. At the same time, we can say with certainty that the teacher at Zuowa Elementary School can "suddenly commit suicide" because he is "unable to endure starvation," and why can't other schools do the same? Even if they don't commit suicide, they will starve to death because they are "unable to endure starvation." I believe it is not uncommon. From this, we can also understand that the bankruptcy of the education field has reached a point that really exceeds the terminology of "pure and poor" —— and even "distress."

However, if we look at it from another perspective, expand our vision, we will think that such a tragedy is very ordinary and expected. Successive natural and man-made disasters, coupled with imperialist aggression, have bankrupted the entire Chinese economy. Because of famine, refugees are everywhere. Guanyin soil and tree bark have replaced all food. Starvation is commonplace. Suicide due to starvation is of course not uncommon. However, the so-called "not uncommon" does not mean "serves you right" or ignoring it. On the contrary, precisely because it is not uncommon, precisely because it is commonplace, we should consider it a serious problem.

The teacher's suicide due to starvation is because education fees are bankrupt, which is because the entire national economy is bankrupt. However, this entire economic bankruptcy is due to the continuous and multi-faceted aggression and exploitation by imperialism, and also due to the unsoundness of the entire economic structure. Therefore, from this tragedy, we should not only recognize the current situation of the education field's產, but also not forget the quyzhuang of this semi-colonial country. As for the method of making up for this defect, of course, only by targeting the root cause of this problem can we have the most correct countermeasure.

Traveling 229

— Fei Xiangdong

During that summer vacation, I set out from home and arrived in Singapore, then transferred to a ship to come to Shanghai for the entrance examination. I took the "Conte Rosso" mail ship, which traveled at a speed of seven [days], crossing the Indian Ocean to reach Shanghai. Throughout this entire week-long voyage, I brought my mandolin to avoid loneliness. Thinking of the moonlit nights at sea, bathing in a kind of white light on the deck, quietly plucking the strings while the waves kept time, what a memorable scene it was.

After boarding the ship, I moved my luggage into the reserved second-class economy cabin, where I met an old man, at least fifty years old, whose graying hair and eyebrow wrinkles were clearly etched in my vision. He had already made his berth and nodded to me, revealing a kind smile. After a while, he approached me again and asked where I was going; because the "Conte Rosso" was first going to Hong Kong before heading to Shanghai. While taking out my daily necessities, I chatted with him; naturally, he learned all about where I was from and about going to Shanghai to take the university entrance exam.

"That's the best thing to do," he said. "Young people should study hard. My eldest son loved to study, but it's a pity he was sent to a tailor shop to be an apprentice at the age of fifteen. Of course, that's because I didn't have the money to provide for him. Later, he said he always resented me for not giving him more opportunities to seek knowledge, which is why he became a tailor. You are fortunate, young man. You must study hard in Shanghai."

What he said was entirely the words of an elder. I listened attentively, without answering him. He noticed my mandolin, reached out to pick it up and looked at it for a while, then curiously plucked it and said to me:

"What is this? Is it called a mandolin? You must love music very much."

"Yes." I nodded.

After the ship set sail, we were together every day, and we talked even more. He loved to listen to my mandolin: we sat together on the deck at the bow of the ship, the moon was full and round, and the sea was calm, truly a rare and beautiful night! So I began to play: playing, the sound of the mandolin, low and carrying a sense of melancholy, floated around the deck. I watched the old man, who half-closed his eyes, completely forgetting everything, letting the music of the mandolin intoxicate him. When my tune stopped and the air immediately returned to silence, he seemed to wake up suddenly from a dream, staring at my face with wide eyes, without saying a word for a long time.

But then, he shifted his body, "You play very well!" he said, tilting his head back, as if trying to find something from the moon, which made me feel that this old man was a bit strange. However, on another night, it was already past nine o'clock, still on that deck, the old man told me a story from his youth.

"Your mandolin has brought back too many memories; I am old and useless, but when I think of Simena, I feel comforted. She was a mixed-race girl commonly seen in Singapore; thirty years ago, we were in love. She played the mandolin very well; we sat together every day, singing songs. Later, her father forced her to marry an Englishman; since then, I have never seen her; nor have I received any news about her."

That's when I understood. The reason my mandolin evoked such sadness in this old man was because he had once had a love story...

He disembarked when the ship reached Hong Kong. He was from Taishan and was going to take a train to Guangzhou. We shook hands warmly at the Kowloon Pier, and the fine drizzle fell on our heads, adding a kind of indescribable sadness of parting.

"Studying is the most wonderful thing, go ahead!" he said to me, but his voice trembled a little. "My eldest son resents me for not giving him the opportunity to study... Study hard and diligently in Shanghai, don't waste your precious youth... Well, goodbye!"

Now, four years have passed, and I have not forgotten this journey. As for that old man, I know nothing about him—I wish him good health!

— Xue

Country folk say: Even the criminals in the city are more arrogant than the gods in the countryside!

A Visit to Lida Chicken Farm 230

(Special Report from This Newspaper) Lida Academy has a considerable history. It has not only made many contributions to social academics, but also made many elaborations on agricultural and pastoral undertakings.

Regarding agriculture and animal husbandry, in addition to a chicken farm in Jiangwan, it also has a horticultural farm and a rural service department in Nanxiang, as well as a bee farm in Songjiang and Jiaxing. Moreover, it also has considerable connections and relationships with agricultural colleges in various places.

Yesterday, in order to understand the situation of the farm's chicken farming business, I and Bingzhong made a special trip to visit it. At that time, we were sincerely entertained by Mr. Guo, the farm manager, and he explained everything in detail, so the impression gained was quite a lot.

The farm occupies a total area of ​​25 mu. In addition to more than a dozen wooden chicken coops, many fruit trees such as peach and apricot trees are planted, as well as milk vetch and vegetables. Peach and apricot trees can already be harvested. Milk vetch is used for bees to collect honey (because bees are also raised on the farm), while vegetables are all chicken feed. In addition, various flowers and miscellaneous trees are also planted. Therefore, this is not only a chicken farm, but also simply a very good horticultural farm.

There are currently six types of chickens here, namely: "Leghorn", "Rhode Island Red", Italian breed. "Barred Plymouth Rock", American breed. "Tiger Chicken", Turkish breed. "Hybrid", which is a cross between a Leghorn rooster and a Xiaoshan hen from our country. "Xiaoshan Chicken" is a pure Xiaoshan chicken that has not been mixed. There are about 300 chickens in total. Each strong rooster can mate with about ten hens, but because each rooster has a different physique, random mating is not allowed and they must be raised in separate groups. Each group has a chicken coop, the structure of which is just like a small house. The bottom of the house is about two or three feet above the ground to prevent moisture, and is covered with random straw, which is turned over every day and replaced every seven days. There is a chicken bed against the wall for roosting, with a manure drawer underneath, which is cleaned once a day. There are also divided chicken cabinets next to it, which are prepared for them to lay eggs. Each room has a water basin and a food trough.

After visiting the adult chicken coop, we went to the brooding room. The architecture there is different from the adult chicken coop. It is relatively tall—about the size of three rooms. Brooding inside is divided into five groups, namely, newly hatched and one week, two weeks, three weeks, and eight weeks. There is a stove in the three-week section, and there are also nanny thermometers in the one- and two-week sections; the temperature is about 90 to 100 [degrees]. There are statistical forms on the wall, which must be filled in according to the grid after daily inspection. People manage it day and night, but the food troughs and drinking fountains are specially made.

Chicks often need to bathe in sand, so each room has a sand basin for bathing.

It is said that the best chicken breed in China is Xiaoshan chicken from Zhejiang, and it is also strong, but it does not lay many eggs, and the eggshell is yellow. Although the Italian chicken is not as healthy as the Chinese chicken and is prone to disease, each hen can lay an average of about 300 eggs per year; they do not rest all year round and have no strong appetite, and the eggshell is pure white—originally, the yellow or white of the eggshell has nothing to do with the substance, but when sold, it is often suspected of being an ordinary chicken egg. However, if a Leghorn hen is crossed with a Xiaoshan rooster, it can become an Italian-type chicken with the physique of a Chinese chicken, combining both advantages. However, the first generation of hybrid chickens has slightly yellowish feathers and eggshells; it must be until the third generation that its feathers and eggshells can completely become like Leghorns, and its physique is of course the same as that of Chinese chickens.

The body weight of this kind of chicken is about five or six catties for hens and seven or eight catties for roosters. Each hen lays eggs for up to six years, and the mating of roosters is also only six years.

Turkish chickens are not raised for laying eggs, but are specifically for meat; it is said that their taste is very delicious. Hens are very small, but roosters weigh as much as twenty or thirty pounds each. Their shape is very scary. According to Mr. Guo, they can guard the night, and whenever they encounter strangers, they will definitely crow wildly.

Later, Mr. Guo led us to his office—that was four rooms in a row, the middle one being the reception room, the one on the left being the office and a hatching room, and the one on the right being the feed room. The reception room was lined with many specimens and regulations of chicken breeds from various countries, and the hatching room had three hot water incubators and one table incubator. The hot water incubator can incubate 250 eggs at the same time each time, and the table incubator can incubate 50 eggs each time; this is completely done using scientific methods. Each time from the start of incubation to the hatching of the chickens takes three weeks, and the most suitable incubation period of the year is spring and autumn, because the climate is too cold or too hot at other times, so it is not suitable.

In terms of feed, barley, wheat bran, and corn flour are usually the main food, in addition to milk powder, bone meal, fish meal, meat meal, oyster shell powder, silkworm chrysalis, etc. As for chicks, chick powder feed and hatching powder feed are used separately, but vegetables and green grass are also essential daily food.

Finally, Mr. Guo said that they originally had more than 2,000 chickens before January 28th. The farm was later destroyed by the war, so these more than 2,000 chickens also sacrificed together in the artillery fire. Although the farm was immediately restored after the war; but a year ago, because the people managing the farm did not know how to do it, it has not yet recovered its former appearance. Mr. Guo was transferred here last year. He is now planning to distribute these chickens to the countryside for trial breeding to see the results. If there is no obstacle in breeding, they will prepare to universally improve and promote it.

Currently, in addition to Mr. Guo, there are also five or six workers who specialize in managing chicken farming.

Unfinished Writing (Continued) 231

— Shi Feng

I saw Lao Feng again a week later on an evening at a public lecture hall.

He held my hand tightly, shaking it as if grabbing a relative. Then, we sat in a corner. Because there were still about thirty minutes before the meeting, we started talking. Naturally, I inquired about his week's life situation.

"I haven't done anything," he shook his head, saying with some emotion: "I don't want to do anything anymore!..."

Looking at that Barbusse-like profile, I was very surprised, why did he become so sentimental? Usually a happy, cheerful person who writes and talks, how could he say such words today? I couldn't help but ask him: "What's wrong?"

"It's not that I don't want to do it anymore, do you know what my passion has earned me?"

Immediately, the faces of Bin and his other friends with satirical smiles appeared before my eyes. Those smiling faces were like bowstrings, forcefully shooting sharp arrows outward, each one hitting Lao Feng's weak heart. Feng, sitting next to me, his painful face, under the dim light, barely supported this pain, laughing with a low nasal tone.

What was placed before my face was truly an unparalleled problem, how could I comfort his pained heart?

"Don't be like this, you can continue to write well, the readers will not fail to appreciate your heart. They will definitely understand an author. You write well, even if there is no place to publish, it is good for us to read it. In fact, your life does not need稿費to maintain..."

The lecture was about to begin, so I had to stop talking. He was also silent.

When the meeting broke up, we parted hands. I advised him not to be discouraged. He shook my hand with great emotion and left. I also returned home.

It was not until three weeks later that I met him. But he had become even worse. He had become a person who only knew how to talk empty words. For example, when he saw me, he asked: "Have you learned the new writing system?" Then he said a lot about the advantages of the new writing system, etc. However, he was a person who had not learned the new writing system. Sometimes, he asked me if I had written any articles, and encouraged me, but his works were not only not completed, but he didn't even move his pen. He changed in people's indifference. Although that way of using a low nasal tone to laugh remained.

Mother 232

— Dong Guang

When my father, who was smuggling salt, was beaten to death by the salt patrol, my mother, on a winter night, climbed into the Ma family's woods and hanged herself. She was rescued by the forest ranger and brought home, and she resumed the hard days that followed. The endless torment crushed this strong woman who grew up in the fields.

In that year, my eighteen-year-old brother, with a vague desire for revenge, joined the army. Since then, he disappeared like a shooting star, never to be heard from again. Relying on a strong body, my mother cranked the pulley day and night for others, watering the radishes or pumpkins in the vegetable plots. When the wheat ripened or the autumn harvest season came, when the sky showed a little gray and the chickens had not yet crowed, she quietly walked out of the village carrying a willow basket, to the small river, looking for the ford where livestock carts crossed the river during the day. She was not afraid of the cold, quiet river water after a night. She lightly stepped onto the opposite bank of the river, patrolling the fields, probing whether the watchman was already asleep in the straw nest. If she saw those guys who specialized in bullying poor old women like her, guarding the edge of the field with their drowsy eyes and carrying big sticks like bears, she would climb into the stone cave under the river embankment, peeking out from the broken sluice gate, waiting until the watchman had completed that circle and returned to the nest, his snoring rumbling. Then she would crouch like a mouse, working swiftly along the edge of the field.

In the summer, she would use a small, sharp sickle to cut some golden wheat ears. In the autumn, she would happily select and steal the red sorghum, the yellow foxtail millet ears, and the snow-like cotton... Sometimes, forgetting herself a little too much, the noise would alert the watchman. He would pick up his scary, thick stick and chase after her. At this point, if she could run away, she would risk her life to climb up the embankment and roll down like a large stone. When she dragged her muddy body to the south bank of the river, things would be considered calm.

Life flowed like an endless stream, and she grew older and older. During the harvest season, although she still had to steal some of the landlords' crops, she was often caught by the watchman. There was no second time. She was beaten or begged for mercy. Those fierce men like dogs snatched the basket away very simply, and angrily whipped the old woman, who was as thin as a bundle of firewood, several times, cursing a string of epithets and filthy words, and then whistled away.

At night, she limped home, dragging her beaten, swollen legs, and lay down on the bed, sighing one after another, cursing her son and her fate, until tears flowed from her dry old eyes. After a moment of silent rest, she sat up again, lit the small black magnetic oil lamp, the flame flickering, and she kept turning her right hand, the wooden crutch of the spinning wheel turning with her chicken-claw-like fingers. On her left hand, she held a strip of white cotton, sending it to the spindle one by one, the spinning wheel humming with the sound of the wind, softly, monotonously echoing in the small house. When the chickens in the yard crowed for a long time, and the sound of carts going to the market in the distance came from the village road, she sighed gloomily, finished the last cotton strip in her hand, put her hand down, yawned, rubbed the corners of her eyes, which were covered with large pieces of white sleep, with a pair of bony hands, lay down, pulled over the torn blue cloth quilt, and slept like a dog.

Broadcasting program broadcasting script

Suzhou People (14) 233

— Gu Wenzong

Jinghong My bread just now was vitamin bread made by the nephew of the French bread king using the most scientific method; the beef I ate was made by the grandson of the German beef king, who personally cooked the nourishing holy product "Vitamin Chicken Juice Beef", so I am now so nourished that I speak big words (laughs after speaking)

Jingya Don't talk nonsense, where did these advertising adjectives come from?

Lihong If I don't say that, I'm afraid the passengers on the train will go to eat cheap and delicious British food because the beef noodles are not sanitary,

Jingya Isn't eating cheap and delicious British food much better than eating those sanitary beef breads?

Jinghong That's right, in this way, British food will become prosperous because of the way the advertisement is promoted, and conversely, the beef bread business will be ignored because of the attack of the rich ladies!

Lihong That's not necessarily true. People who eat big dishes always eat big dishes. People who eat beef bread will never change to eat big dishes because of publicity. This is based on each person's economic strength. It is by no means that advertising can dominate,

Ballad Singing 234

He Yunfang He Qinfang Double Pearl Phoenix

Chinese-Western (1040) 1:00 PM to 1:12 PM

Opening Piece "Wang Xifeng Sets a Scheme"

Dreaming of the Red Mansion, talking about the Wang family. Sister Feng is too frivolous. She is wanton and unrestrained, no one cares. Single-mindedly, she loves beauty, is greedy for money, and busy with schemes. Most ridiculous. Jia Rui has ideas and tries to take liberties. Repeatedly seduces, wanting Phoenix to seek Phoenix. Who knows Xifeng's heart is poisonous. So she called Rong to discuss with her second nephew. Everyone creates a poisonous prelude, a scheme of longing. Most regrettable, there is no public virtue and a lack of righteousness. Rui-ge is greedy for beauty and happy. In the evening, secretly enters the walled house. Stealthily waits for the door to open in the alley. How can the bone-chilling wind be resisted. Suddenly, he hears the window opening upstairs and his heart is happy. Initially unexpected, a torrent of foul water tastes foul. Jia Rui is, soaked all over. He is planning and running away in a panic. Annoying Jia Rong holds a torch and comes out. Grabbing him on the spot, wanting to send him to the officials. Jia Zhen comes out to mediate. Forcing him to write a promissory note. From then on, Rui-ge becomes sick. His mind is confused and he lies on the bed. So, he takes the life of the young lord in an instant.
